\secdivider{Section S13}{Exception Handling}{cE}{cE}
\markboth{S13 --- Exception Handling}{}
\label{sec:S13}
\titleformat{\section}{\large\bfseries\color{cE}}{}{0em}{}[\titlerule]
\section{S13 --- Exception Handling}

\begin{enumerate}
\item What is the problem in the following C++ program? Rewrite using exception handling:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++]
#include <iostream>
using namespace std;
int divide() {
    int d = 0;
    int a = 10 / d;
    return a;
}
int main() { cout << divide() << endl; return 0; }
\end{lstlisting}
\mk{2+5}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2023--24}

%% -- Q1 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Division by Zero: Problem and Fix with Exception Handling}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]

\textbf{Problem:} \texttt{d = 0} causes \textbf{division by zero},
which is undefined behaviour in C++. The program may crash or produce
garbage output with no graceful error message.

\textbf{Fixed version using exception handling:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++]
#include <iostream>
#include <stdexcept>
using namespace std;

int divide() {
    int d = 0;
    if (d == 0)
        throw runtime_error("Division by zero!");
    int a = 10 / d;
    return a;
}

int main() {
    try {
        cout << divide() << endl;
    } catch (const runtime_error& e) {
        cerr << "Caught exception: " << e.what() << endl;
    }
    return 0;
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
Caught exception: Division by zero!
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}




\item Consider a class \texttt{BankAccount}. Write: (i) \texttt{InvalidAmountException};\\ (ii) \texttt{InsufficientBalanceException}; (iii) complete \texttt{BankAccount}/\texttt{Account} class: \mk{15}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2022--23}

%% -- Q13 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- BankAccount with InvalidAmount and InsufficientBalance Exceptions}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class InvalidAmountException extends Exception {
    InvalidAmountException(double amt) {
        super("Amount must be positive. Got: " + amt);
    }
}

class InsufficientBalanceException extends Exception {
    InsufficientBalanceException(double needed, double available) {
        super("Need " + needed + " but only " + available + " available");
    }
}

class BankAccount {
    private String owner;
    private double balance;

    BankAccount(String owner, double initialBalance)
            throws InvalidAmountException {
        if (initialBalance < 0)
            throw new InvalidAmountException(initialBalance);
        this.owner   = owner;
        this.balance = initialBalance;
    }

    void deposit(double amt) throws InvalidAmountException {
        if (amt <= 0) throw new InvalidAmountException(amt);
        balance += amt;
    }

    void withdraw(double amt)
            throws InvalidAmountException, InsufficientBalanceException {
        if (amt <= 0) throw new InvalidAmountException(amt);
        if (amt > balance)
            throw new InsufficientBalanceException(amt, balance);
        balance -= amt;
    }

    double getBalance() { return balance; }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        try {
            BankAccount acc = new BankAccount("Alice", 500);
            acc.deposit(200);
            System.out.println("Balance: " + acc.getBalance()); // 700
            acc.withdraw(900); // throws InsufficientBalanceException
        } catch (InvalidAmountException e) {
            System.out.println("Invalid: " + e.getMessage());
        } catch (InsufficientBalanceException e) {
            System.out.println("Insufficient: " + e.getMessage());
        }
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}



\item Write the name of the five keywords in Java dedicated to exception handling. \mk{15}

Consider a class named \texttt{BankAccount} with the following information:
\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{double balance} -- the balance of the account
    \item \texttt{void init(double amount)} -- this method sets the amount as the initial balance
    \item \texttt{void debit(double amount)} -- this method subtracts the amount from the balance
    \item \texttt{void credit(double amount)} -- this method adds the amount directly to the balance
\end{itemize}
The amount provided in the above methods can't be negative. The balance of the account can't also be negative.

Write Java code for the following:
\begin{enumerate}
    \item A custom exception (\texttt{InvalidAmountException}) that triggers when the given amount is negative and shows the message `The given amount can't be negative' and the given amount.
    \item A custom exception (\texttt{InsufficientBalanceException}) that triggers when the balance goes negative and shows the message `The account balance can't be negative' and the current balance.
    \item The complete \texttt{Account} (or \texttt{BankAccount}) class to trigger these exceptions when needed.
\end{enumerate}
You don't need to write any main method.
\yr{CSE 107 | 2016--17, 2022--23}

%% -- Q12 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- BankAccount Class with Custom Exceptions}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]

\textbf{Five keywords for exception handling in Java:} 
\texttt{try}, \texttt{catch}, \texttt{finally}, \texttt{throw}, and \texttt{throws}.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// i. Custom exception for negative amounts
class InvalidAmountException extends Exception {
    public InvalidAmountException(double amount) {
        super("The given amount can't be negative: " + amount);
    }
}

// ii. Custom exception for negative balance
class InsufficientBalanceException extends Exception {
    public InsufficientBalanceException(double currentBalance) {
        super("The account balance can't be negative: " + currentBalance);
    }
}

// iii. The complete BankAccount class
class BankAccount {
    private double balance;

    void init(double amount) throws InvalidAmountException {
        if (amount < 0) {
            throw new InvalidAmountException(amount);
        }
        this.balance = amount;
    }

    void debit(double amount) throws InvalidAmountException, InsufficientBalanceException {
        if (amount < 0) {
            throw new InvalidAmountException(amount);
        }
        if (this.balance - amount < 0) {
            throw new InsufficientBalanceException(this.balance - amount);
        }
        this.balance -= amount;
    }

    void credit(double amount) throws InvalidAmountException {
        if (amount < 0) {
            throw new InvalidAmountException(amount);
        }
        this.balance += amount;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\item Consider a class named Inventory with the following information: \hfill \textbf{(10)}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{double stock} - the stock of the inventory
    \item \texttt{double minStock} - the minimum stock of the inventory
    \item \texttt{void setInitialStock(double amount)} - this method sets the amount as the initial stock
    \item \texttt{void addToInventory(double amount)} - this method adds the amount to the stock
    \item \texttt{void removeFromInventory(double amount)} - this method subtracts the amount from the stock
\end{itemize}
The amount provided in the above four methods can't be negative. The stock of the inventory can't also be below the minimum stock.

Write Java code for the following:
\begin{itemize}
    \item[(i)] A custom exception named \texttt{InvalidStockAmountException} with appropriate parameters that triggers when the given amount is negative and shows the message 'The given stock amount can't be negative'.
    \item[(ii)] A custom exception named \texttt{InvalidInventoryStockException} with appropriate parameters that triggers when the stock goes below the minimum stock and shows the message 'The stock can't be less than the minimum stock'.
    \item[(iii)] The complete \texttt{Inventory} class to trigger these exceptions when needed. You don't need to write any main method.
\end{itemize}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2020--21}

%% -- Q16 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Inventory Class with Custom Exceptions}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// (i) Custom exception for negative stock amounts
class InvalidStockAmountException extends Exception {
    public InvalidStockAmountException() {
        super("The given stock amount can't be negative.");
    }
}

// (ii) Custom exception for stock dropping below minimum limits
class InvalidInventoryStockException extends Exception {
    public InvalidInventoryStockException() {
        super("The stock can't be less than the minimum stock.");
    }
}

// (iii) The complete Inventory class matching specified requirements
class Inventory {
    private double stock;
    private double minStock;

    // Constructor to set fields
    public Inventory(double minStock) {
        this.minStock = minStock;
        this.stock = 0.0;
    }

    public void setInitialStock(double amount) throws InvalidStockAmountException, InvalidInventoryStockException {
        if (amount < 0) {
            throw new InvalidStockAmountException();
        }
        if (amount < minStock) {
            throw new InvalidInventoryStockException();
        }
        this.stock = amount;
    }

    public void addToInventory(double amount) throws InvalidStockAmountException {
        if (amount < 0) {
            throw new InvalidStockAmountException();
        }
        this.stock += amount;
    }

    public void removeFromInventory(double amount) throws InvalidStockAmountException, InvalidInventoryStockException {
        if (amount < 0) {
            throw new InvalidStockAmountException();
        }
        if (this.stock - amount < minStock) {
            throw new InvalidInventoryStockException();
        }
        this.stock -= amount;
    }

    // Getters for inspecting the states
    public double getStock() {
        return stock;
    }

    public double getMinStock() {
        return minStock;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\item Explain the use of \texttt{try} and \texttt{catch} in C++ with appropriate examples. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2015--16}

%% -- Q2 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- try and catch in C++}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]

\textbf{try block:} Encloses code that might throw an exception.
\textbf{catch block:} Handles a specific type of exception thrown from the try block.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=C++]
#include <iostream>
#include <stdexcept>
using namespace std;

double safeDivide(double a, double b) {
    if (b == 0)
        throw runtime_error("Cannot divide by zero");
    return a / b;
}

int main() {
    // Example 1: catching a runtime_error
    try {
        cout << safeDivide(10, 2) << endl;  // 5
        cout << safeDivide(10, 0) << endl;  // throws
    } catch (const runtime_error& e) {
        cout << "runtime_error: " << e.what() << endl;
    }

    // Example 2: multiple catch blocks
    try {
        int choice = 2;
        if (choice == 1) throw 42;           // throw int
        if (choice == 2) throw string("err"); // throw string
    } catch (int i) {
        cout << "Caught int: " << i << endl;
    } catch (const string& s) {
        cout << "Caught string: " << s << endl;
    } catch (...) {
        cout << "Caught unknown exception" << endl;
    }

    return 0;
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
5
runtime_error: Cannot divide by zero
Caught string: err
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}



\item Show the hierarchical relation among \texttt{Throwable}, \texttt{Exception}, \texttt{RuntimeException} and \texttt{Error} classes. Write a custom exception \texttt{AuthFailureException}. Also write an \texttt{Authenticate()} method that will throw \texttt{AuthFailureException} on failure. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2015--16}

%% -- Q7 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Java Exception Hierarchy and Custom Exception Handling}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]

\textbf{Hierarchical Relation:}

In Java, the exception handling framework is structured as a class hierarchy rooted at \texttt{java.lang.Object}. The four core classes are related as shown below:

\begin{verbatim}
java.lang.Object
   |
   +-- java.lang.Throwable
         |
         +-- java.lang.Error (Unchecked/Fatal JVM errors)
         |     |-- OutOfMemoryError
         |     +-- StackOverflowError
         |
         +-- java.lang.Exception (Checked/Application exceptions)
               |-- IOException
               |-- SQLException
               |
               +-- java.lang.RuntimeException (Unchecked/Logic errors)
                     |-- NullPointerException
                     +-- ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException
\end{verbatim}

\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{\texttt{Throwable}:} The ultimate superclass of all errors and exceptions in the Java language. Only objects that are instances of this class (or one of its subclasses) can be thrown by the JVM or via the \texttt{throw} statement.
    \item \textbf{\texttt{Error}:} A subclass of \texttt{Throwable} that indicates serious, unrecoverable problems that a reasonable application should not try to catch (e.g., system crashes or resource exhaustion).
    \item \textbf{\texttt{Exception}:} A subclass of \texttt{Throwable} that indicates conditions that a reasonable application might want to catch and handle. These are typically compile-time "checked" exceptions.
    \item \textbf{\texttt{RuntimeException}:} A major subclass of \texttt{Exception} that represents "unchecked" exceptions or programming flaws (such as null pointer dereferences or array index violations) occurring at runtime.
\end{itemize}

\medskip
\textbf{Java Implementation:}

Below is the implementation of the custom exception \texttt{AuthFailureException} and the required \texttt{Authenticate()} validation method.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// Custom checked exception extending the base Exception class
class AuthFailureException extends Exception {
    // Constructor that accepts a detailed error message
    public AuthFailureException(String message) {
        super(message);
    }
}

class UserAuthenticator {
    // Authenticate method that validates credentials and declares throwing the custom exception
    public void Authenticate(String username, String password) throws AuthFailureException {
        // Simple mock credentials check
        String correctUsername = "admin";
        String correctPassword = "password123";

        if (!correctUsername.equals(username) || !correctPassword.equals(password)) {
            // Throwing the custom exception on failure
            throw new AuthFailureException("Authentication failed: Invalid credentials for user '" + username + "'.");
        }

        System.out.println("Authentication successful for user: " + username);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Write your own \texttt{TwoDimException} that is thrown when the determinant of a matrix is zero. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2015--16}

%% -- Q14 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- TwoDimException for Zero Determinant}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class TwoDimException extends Exception {
    TwoDimException() {
        super("Matrix is singular: determinant is zero.");
    }
}

class Matrix2x2 {
    private double[][] m;

    Matrix2x2(double a, double b, double c, double d) {
        m = new double[][]{{a, b}, {c, d}};
    }

    double determinant() {
        return m[0][0] * m[1][1] - m[0][1] * m[1][0];
    }

    // Returns inverse; throws TwoDimException if det == 0
    Matrix2x2 inverse() throws TwoDimException {
        double det = determinant();
        if (det == 0) throw new TwoDimException();
        return new Matrix2x2(
             m[1][1] / det, -m[0][1] / det,
            -m[1][0] / det,  m[0][0] / det);
    }

    @Override
    public String toString() {
        return String.format("[[%.2f, %.2f], [%.2f, %.2f]]",
                             m[0][0], m[0][1], m[1][0], m[1][1]);
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Matrix2x2 m1 = new Matrix2x2(2, 1, 5, 3);
        Matrix2x2 m2 = new Matrix2x2(1, 2, 2, 4); // det = 0

        try {
            System.out.println("Inverse of m1: " + m1.inverse());
            System.out.println("Inverse of m2: " + m2.inverse());
        } catch (TwoDimException e) {
            System.out.println("Error: " + e.getMessage());
        }
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
Inverse of m1: [[3.00, -1.00], [-5.00, 2.00]]
Error: Matrix is singular: determinant is zero.
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}



\item Consider a \texttt{MyStack} class with \texttt{push(Object)}, \texttt{pop()}, \texttt{top()}, \texttt{isEmpty()}. \texttt{pop()} and \texttt{top()} throw \texttt{StackEmptyException}; \texttt{push()} throws \texttt{StackFullException}. Write the custom exceptions and the \texttt{MyStack} class. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2014--15}

%% -- Q15 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- MyStack with StackEmptyException and StackFullException}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class StackEmptyException extends Exception {
    StackEmptyException() { super("Stack is empty"); }
}

class StackFullException extends Exception {
    StackFullException() { super("Stack is full"); }
}

class MyStack {
    private Object[] data;
    private int top;
    private int capacity;

    MyStack(int capacity) {
        this.capacity = capacity;
        data = new Object[capacity];
        top  = -1;
    }

    boolean isEmpty() { return top == -1; }
    boolean isFull()  { return top == capacity - 1; }

    void push(Object obj) throws StackFullException {
        if (isFull()) throw new StackFullException();
        data[++top] = obj;
    }

    Object pop() throws StackEmptyException {
        if (isEmpty()) throw new StackEmptyException();
        return data[top--];
    }

    Object top() throws StackEmptyException {
        if (isEmpty()) throw new StackEmptyException();
        return data[top];
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        MyStack s = new MyStack(3);
        try {
            s.push("A"); s.push("B"); s.push("C");
            System.out.println("Top: " + s.top());   // C
            System.out.println("Pop: " + s.pop());   // C
            s.push("D");
            s.push("E"); // StackFullException
        } catch (StackFullException e) {
            System.out.println("Full: " + e.getMessage());
        } catch (StackEmptyException e) {
            System.out.println("Empty: " + e.getMessage());
        }
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}



\item Write a program that throws and catches an exception when the value of a variable is greater than 1000. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2012--13}

%% -- Q3 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Throw and Catch When Value $>$ 1000}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class ValueTooLargeException extends Exception {
    ValueTooLargeException(int val) {
        super("Value " + val + " exceeds 1000");
    }
}

class ThrowDemo {
    static void check(int val) throws ValueTooLargeException {
        if (val > 1000)
            throw new ValueTooLargeException(val);
        System.out.println("Value OK: " + val);
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        int[] tests = {500, 1001, 999, 2000};
        for (int v : tests) {
            try {
                check(v);
            } catch (ValueTooLargeException e) {
                System.out.println("Exception: " + e.getMessage());
            }
        }
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
Value OK: 500
Exception: Value 1001 exceeds 1000
Value OK: 999
Exception: Value 2000 exceeds 1000
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}



\item Write a program that illustrates re-throwing an exception. \mk{4}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2011--12}

%% -- Q5 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Re-throwing an Exception}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class RethrowDemo {
    static void level2() throws Exception {
        throw new Exception("Original exception from level2");
    }

    static void level1() throws Exception {
        try {
            level2();
        } catch (Exception e) {
            System.out.println("level1 caught: " + e.getMessage());
            System.out.println("level1 re-throwing...");
            throw e;   // re-throw the same exception
        }
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        try {
            level1();
        } catch (Exception e) {
            System.out.println("main caught: " + e.getMessage());
        }
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
level1 caught: Original exception from level2
level1 re-throwing...
main caught: Original exception from level2
\end{verbatim}
Re-throwing allows a method to partially handle an exception (e.g.,
log it) and then pass it up to a higher-level handler.
\end{tcolorbox}



\item What are the keywords associated with exception handling in Java? Write the use of each keyword. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2011--12}

%% -- Q6 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Java Exception Handling Keywords}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]

Java has \textbf{five} keywords for exception handling:

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}ll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Keyword} & \textbf{Use} \\
\midrule
\texttt{try}     & Wraps code that may throw an exception \\
\texttt{catch}   & Handles a specific exception type \\
\texttt{finally} & Runs always, whether or not an exception occurred \\
\texttt{throw}   & Explicitly throws an exception object \\
\texttt{throws}  & Declares which checked exceptions a method may propagate \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class KeywordsDemo {
    // 'throws' declares checked exception
    static int divide(int a, int b) throws ArithmeticException {
        if (b == 0)
            throw new ArithmeticException("div by zero"); // 'throw'
        return a / b;
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        try {                        // 'try'
            System.out.println(divide(10, 2));
            System.out.println(divide(10, 0));
        } catch (ArithmeticException e) {  // 'catch'
            System.out.println("Caught: " + e.getMessage());
        } finally {                  // 'finally'
            System.out.println("Finally block always runs");
        }
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
5
Caught: div by zero
Finally block always runs
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}



\item In JVM, when is a \texttt{ClassCastException} thrown? How can we avoid it? \mk{5+2}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2010--11}

%% -- Q8 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- ClassCastException: When and How to Avoid}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]

\textbf{When is it thrown?}

A \texttt{ClassCastException} is thrown at run time when the JVM
attempts to cast an object to a type it is \emph{not} an instance of.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
Object obj = "Hello";      // obj actually holds a String
Integer i  = (Integer) obj; // ClassCastException at run time!
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{How to avoid it:}

Use the \texttt{instanceof} operator to check the actual type before
casting.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
Object obj = "Hello";

if (obj instanceof Integer) {
    Integer i = (Integer) obj;
    System.out.println("Integer: " + i);
} else {
    System.out.println("Not an Integer: " + obj.getClass().getName());
}
// Output: Not an Integer: java.lang.String
\end{lstlisting}

Using generics also prevents \texttt{ClassCastException} at compile
time by enforcing type safety without explicit casts.
\end{tcolorbox}



\item Explain three different usages of the keyword \texttt{finally} with examples. \mk{9}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2010--11}

%% -- Q9 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Three Usages of \texttt{finally}}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]

\textbf{Usage 1 --- Resource cleanup (always close resources):}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
FileReader fr = null;
try {
    fr = new FileReader("file.txt");
    // read file ...
} catch (IOException e) {
    System.out.println("IO Error: " + e.getMessage());
} finally {
    if (fr != null) try { fr.close(); } catch (IOException ignored) {}
    System.out.println("FileReader closed.");
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Usage 2 --- Runs even when no exception occurs:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
try {
    System.out.println("No exception here");
} catch (Exception e) {
    System.out.println("This won't run");
} finally {
    System.out.println("Finally runs anyway");  // always executes
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Usage 3 --- Runs even after a return statement in try:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
static int getValue() {
    try {
        return 10;            // return is deferred
    } finally {
        System.out.println("finally before actual return");
    }
}
// Output: "finally before actual return", then returns 10
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}



\item Write down the syntax used for Java's `catch or declare' strategy of exception handling. \mk{7}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2010--11}

%% -- Q10 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Catch or Declare Strategy}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]

Java's \textbf{``catch or declare''} rule applies to \emph{checked}
exceptions: any method that may throw a checked exception must either
\textbf{(a) catch} it locally or \textbf{(b) declare} it with
\texttt{throws}.

\textbf{Option A --- Catch it (handle locally):}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
void readFile(String path) {
    try {
        FileReader fr = new FileReader(path);
        // ... use fr ...
    } catch (IOException e) {
        System.out.println("Handled: " + e.getMessage());
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Option B --- Declare it (propagate to caller):}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
void readFile(String path) throws IOException {
    FileReader fr = new FileReader(path); // not caught here
    // ... use fr ...
}

// Caller must then catch or declare IOException
void caller() throws IOException {
    readFile("data.txt");
}
\end{lstlisting}

Unchecked exceptions (\texttt{RuntimeException} and its subclasses)
are \emph{exempt} from this rule --- they may be thrown without
declaration.
\end{tcolorbox}



\item How can we create a user-defined exception type? Give an example. \mk{4}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2010--11}

%% -- Q11 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Creating a User-Defined Exception}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]

Extend \texttt{Exception} (for checked) or \texttt{RuntimeException}
(for unchecked) and provide a constructor that passes a message to
\texttt{super()}.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// User-defined checked exception
class AgeOutOfRangeException extends Exception {
    AgeOutOfRangeException(int age) {
        super("Age " + age + " is out of valid range (0-150)");
    }
}

class Person {
    private int age;

    void setAge(int age) throws AgeOutOfRangeException {
        if (age < 0 || age > 150)
            throw new AgeOutOfRangeException(age);
        this.age = age;
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Person p = new Person();
        try {
            p.setAge(25);   // OK
            p.setAge(200);  // throws
        } catch (AgeOutOfRangeException e) {
            System.out.println("Caught: " + e.getMessage());
        }
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
Caught: Age 200 is out of valid range (0-150)
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}



\item Write a program that illustrates the application of multiple \texttt{catch} statements. \mk{5}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2007--08}

%% -- Q4 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Multiple catch Statements}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class MultiCatchDemo {
    static void test(int choice) {
        try {
            if (choice == 1)
                throw new ArithmeticException("Arithmetic error");
            else if (choice == 2)
                throw new ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException("Bad index");
            else if (choice == 3)
                throw new NullPointerException("Null ref");
            else {
                int[] arr = new int[3];
                arr[5] = 10;  // causes ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException
            }
        } catch (ArithmeticException e) {
            System.out.println("Caught ArithmeticException: "
                               + e.getMessage());
        } catch (ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException e) {
            System.out.println("Caught ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException: "
                               + e.getMessage());
        } catch (NullPointerException e) {
            System.out.println("Caught NullPointerException: "
                               + e.getMessage());
        } catch (Exception e) {
            System.out.println("Caught general Exception: "
                               + e.getMessage());
        }
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        test(1); test(2); test(3); test(4);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
Caught ArithmeticException: Arithmetic error
Caught ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException: Bad index
Caught NullPointerException: Null ref
Caught ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException: Index 5 out of bounds for length 3
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}



\item Suppose you are asked to write \texttt{MyException} that takes a String parameter. When displayed, it shows the String. Write necessary code. \mk{8}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2007--08}

%% -- Q17 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cE!4,colframe=cE,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- MyException with String Parameter}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cE]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class MyException extends Exception {
    private String message;

    MyException(String msg) {
        super(msg);          // pass to Exception
        this.message = msg;
    }

    @Override
    public String toString() {
        return "MyException: " + message;
    }
}

class MyExceptionDemo {
    static void riskyMethod(int x) throws MyException {
        if (x < 0)
            throw new MyException("Negative value not allowed: " + x);
        System.out.println("Value is: " + x);
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        try {
            riskyMethod(5);
            riskyMethod(-3);
        } catch (MyException e) {
            System.out.println(e);           // calls toString()
            System.out.println(e.getMessage()); // from super
        }
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
Value is: 5
MyException: Negative value not allowed: -3
Negative value not allowed: -3
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}




\end{enumerate}

%% S14 — Multithreading & Concurrency
%%══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
\secdivider{Section S14}{Multithreading \& Concurrency}{cF}{cF}
\markboth{S14 --- Multithreading \& Concurrency}{}
\label{sec:S14}
\titleformat{\section}{\large\bfseries\color{cF}}{}{0em}{}[\titlerule]
\section{S14 --- Multithreading \& Concurrency}

\begin{enumerate}

\item Complete the following Java code that finds the summation of a 10000-element integer array using an array of 10 threads in parallel. You cannot write any more classes, but you can add variables, constructors, and other methods. \mk{15}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class ParallelSum implements Runnable {
    // your code here
}

public class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        java.util.Random random = new java.util.Random();
        int[] numbers = new int[10000];
        
        for (int i = 0; i < numbers.length; i++) {
            numbers[i] = random.nextInt(10000);
        }
        
        ParallelSum[] parallelSum = new ParallelSum[10];
        // your code here
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2023--24}

%% ── Answer: ParallelSum skeleton completion ─────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Parallel Sum of 10,000-Element Array (10 Threads)}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

To achieve parallel summation, each \texttt{ParallelSum} instance should be responsible for a subset (chunk) of the array. After the threads finish executing (\texttt{join}), the main thread aggregates the partial sums.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class ParallelSum implements Runnable {
    private int[] numbers;
    private int start;
    private int end;
    private long partialSum;

    // Constructor to assign the array and the bounds for this thread
    public ParallelSum(int[] numbers, int start, int end) {
        this.numbers = numbers;
        this.start = start;
        this.end = end;
        this.partialSum = 0;
    }

    @Override
    public void run() {
        for (int i = start; i < end; i++) {
            partialSum += numbers[i];
        }
    }

    // Method to retrieve the calculated sum for this chunk
    public long getPartialSum() {
        return partialSum;
    }
}

public class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        java.util.Random random = new java.util.Random();
        int[] numbers = new int[10000];
        
        for (int i = 0; i < numbers.length; i++) {
            numbers[i] = random.nextInt(10000);
        }
        
        ParallelSum[] parallelSum = new ParallelSum[10];
        Thread[] threads = new Thread[10];
        
        int chunkSize = numbers.length / 10; // 1000 elements per thread
        
        // 1. Initialize Runnables and start Threads
        for (int i = 0; i < 10; i++) {
            int start = i * chunkSize;
            int end = start + chunkSize;
            
            parallelSum[i] = new ParallelSum(numbers, start, end);
            threads[i] = new Thread(parallelSum[i]);
            threads[i].start();
        }
        
        long totalSum = 0;
        
        // 2. Wait for threads to finish and aggregate results
        for (int i = 0; i < 10; i++) {
            try {
                threads[i].join(); // Ensure the thread has finished
                totalSum += parallelSum[i].getPartialSum();
            } catch (InterruptedException e) {
                e.printStackTrace();
            }
        }
        
        System.out.println("Total sum = " + totalSum);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Consider the following code. Determine all possible outputs assuming T1 starts first. If two threads execute f0 and f1, will they run in parallel? Why or why not?
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class TestClass {
    public void f0() { synchronized(this) { for(int i=0;i<5;i++) System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName()+" "+i); } }
    public void f1() { synchronized(TestClass.class) { for(int i=0;i<5;i++) System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName()+" "+i); } }
    public synchronized static void f2() { for(int i=0;i<5;i++) System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName()+" "+i); }
    public synchronized static void f3() { for(int i=0;i<5;i++) System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName()+" "+i); }
}
class SynchronizedTest {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        new Thread(new TestClass()::f1, "T1").start();
        new Thread(TestClass::f2, "T2").start();
        new Thread(TestClass::f3, "T3").start();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2023--24}

%% ── Answer: synchronized lock analysis ──────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Lock Analysis: \texttt{f0}, \texttt{f1}, \texttt{f2}, \texttt{f3}}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\textbf{Lock objects used by each method:}

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Method} & \textbf{Lock object} & \textbf{Type} \\
\midrule
\texttt{f0()} & \texttt{this} (instance)        & instance lock \\
\texttt{f1()} & \texttt{TestClass.class}        & class lock \\
\texttt{f2()} & \texttt{TestClass.class} (static sync) & class lock \\
\texttt{f3()} & \texttt{TestClass.class} (static sync) & class lock \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip
\textbf{The three threads in \texttt{main}:}
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=1pt]
  \item \textbf{T1} calls \texttt{f1()} --- acquires the
    \textbf{class lock} (\texttt{TestClass.class}).
  \item \textbf{T2} calls \textbf{static} \texttt{f2()} --- also
    acquires the \textbf{class lock}.
  \item \textbf{T3} calls \textbf{static} \texttt{f3()} --- also
    acquires the \textbf{class lock}.
\end{itemize}

All three threads compete for the \emph{same} lock
(\texttt{TestClass.class}), so \textbf{they cannot run in parallel}.
They execute one at a time in some order.

\medskip
\textbf{Possible outputs} (T1 starts first; T2 and T3 may interleave
after T1 finishes --- all orderings of T2 and T3 are valid):

\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),itemsep=1pt]
  \item T1 runs completely, then T2, then T3.
  \item T1 runs completely, then T3, then T2.
\end{enumerate}

Within each thread's turn the output is always its 5 lines in order
(\texttt{T1 0} \ldots \texttt{T1 4}, etc.).  No interleaving of
individual lines between threads is possible because each holds the
class lock for its entire loop.

\medskip
\textbf{Would \texttt{f0} and \texttt{f1} run in parallel?}

\textbf{Yes} --- if two threads called \texttt{f0} and \texttt{f1}
on the \emph{same} instance, they would still run in parallel because
\texttt{f0} locks on \texttt{this} (the \emph{instance} lock) while
\texttt{f1} locks on \texttt{TestClass.class} (the \emph{class}
lock).  These are two \emph{different} objects, so neither thread
blocks the other.

\end{tcolorbox}

\item What is the problem with the following code? Write 2 different ways to fix it:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class MyThread implements Runnable {
    List<String> list;
    Thread t;
    public MyThread(List<String> list) { this.list = list; t = new Thread(this); t.start(); }
    public void run() { for(int i=1;i<=10000;i++) list.add(String.valueOf(i)); }
}
public class TestSyncArrayList {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception {
        List<String> list = new ArrayList<>();
        MyThread t1 = new MyThread(list), t2 = new MyThread(list);
        t1.t.join(); t2.t.join();
        System.out.println(list.size());
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2023--24}

%% ── Answer: ArrayList race condition fix ────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Race Condition on \texttt{ArrayList}: Problem \& Two Fixes}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\textbf{The problem:}

\texttt{ArrayList} is \textbf{not thread-safe}.  When two threads call
\texttt{list.add()} concurrently, internal array resizing and index
updates can interleave, causing:
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=1pt]
  \item lost updates (final size less than 20{,}000), or
  \item an \texttt{ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} during resize.
\end{itemize}
The printed size is therefore unpredictable and almost never
20{,}000.

\medskip
\textcolor{cF}{\rule{\textwidth}{0.4pt}}
\medskip

\textbf{Fix 1 --- Replace \texttt{ArrayList} with
\texttt{CopyOnWriteArrayList}}

\texttt{CopyOnWriteArrayList} is a thread-safe variant from
\texttt{java.util.concurrent}.  Every write creates a fresh copy of
the internal array, so concurrent \texttt{add()} calls are safe
without explicit locking.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.*;
import java.util.concurrent.CopyOnWriteArrayList;

class MyThread implements Runnable {
    List<String> list;
    Thread t;
    public MyThread(List<String> list) {
        this.list = list;
        t = new Thread(this);
        t.start();
    }
    public void run() {
        for (int i = 1; i <= 10000; i++)
            list.add(String.valueOf(i));
    }
}

public class Fix1 {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception {
        // Use thread-safe list instead of ArrayList
        List<String> list = new CopyOnWriteArrayList<>();
        MyThread t1 = new MyThread(list);
        MyThread t2 = new MyThread(list);
        t1.t.join(); t2.t.join();
        System.out.println(list.size()); // always 20000
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{Fix 2 --- Synchronise the \texttt{add()} call manually}

Keep \texttt{ArrayList} but wrap every \texttt{add()} inside a
\texttt{synchronized} block on the shared list object.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class MyThreadSync implements Runnable {
    List<String> list;
    Thread t;
    public MyThreadSync(List<String> list) {
        this.list = list;
        t = new Thread(this);
        t.start();
    }
    public void run() {
        for (int i = 1; i <= 10000; i++)
            synchronized (list) {          // lock on the shared list
                list.add(String.valueOf(i));
            }
    }
}

public class Fix2 {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws Exception {
        List<String> list = new ArrayList<>();
        MyThreadSync t1 = new MyThreadSync(list);
        MyThreadSync t2 = new MyThreadSync(list);
        t1.t.join(); t2.t.join();
        System.out.println(list.size()); // always 20000
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textit{Note: \texttt{Collections.synchronizedList(new ArrayList<>())}
is also a valid Fix 2 alternative --- it wraps every method with a
synchronized block automatically.}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item You are given a task to find the total count of prime numbers in a randomly generated array of 10{,}000 integers (values 1--5000). Divide work equally among 5 threads. Main thread waits and prints final count. \mk{15}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2022--23}

%% ── Answer: Parallel prime count ────────────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Parallel Prime Count in 10{,}000-Element Array (5 Threads)}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

Each thread inspects 2{,}000 elements of the array for primality.
Partial counts are stored in a shared \texttt{counts[]} array.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public class PrimeCount {

    static boolean isPrime(int n) {
        if (n < 2) return false;
        for (int i = 2; i * i <= n; i++)
            if (n % i == 0) return false;
        return true;
    }

    static class PrimeTask implements Runnable {
        private final int[] arr;
        private final int start, end, id;
        private final int[] counts;

        PrimeTask(int[] arr, int start, int end,
                  int[] counts, int id) {
            this.arr = arr; this.start = start;
            this.end = end; this.counts = counts;
            this.id = id;
        }

        @Override
        public void run() {
            int c = 0;
            for (int i = start; i < end; i++)
                if (isPrime(arr[i])) c++;
            counts[id] = c;
        }
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException {
        int[]  arr    = new int[10000];
        int[]  counts = new int[5];
        java.util.Random rnd = new java.util.Random();
        for (int i = 0; i < arr.length; i++)
            arr[i] = rnd.nextInt(5000) + 1;

        Thread[] threads = new Thread[5];
        int chunk = arr.length / 5; // 2000 each

        for (int i = 0; i < 5; i++) {
            threads[i] = new Thread(new PrimeTask(
                arr, i * chunk, (i + 1) * chunk, counts, i));
            threads[i].start();
        }
        for (Thread t : threads) t.join();

        int total = 0;
        for (int c : counts) total += c;
        System.out.println("Total prime count = " + total);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item You are given the following class. Create threads T1--T5 from main to execute f1, f2, f0, fs1, and fs2. (i) Which threads run in parallel and why? (ii) Which do not? Can restriction R2 be relaxed?
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class ThreadTest {
    public void f0() { for(int i=1;i<500;i++) System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName()+" "+i); }
    public synchronized void f1() { for(int i=1;i<1000;i++) System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName()+" "+i); }
    public synchronized void f2() { for(int i=1;i<1500;i++) System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName()+" "+i); }
    public synchronized static void fs1() { for(int i=1;i<2000;i++) System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName()+" "+i); }
    public synchronized static void fs2() { for(int i=1;i<2500;i++) System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName()+" "+i); }
}
\end{lstlisting}
R1: Cannot change \texttt{ThreadTest}. R2: Can create only one object. \mk{15}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2022--23}

%% ── Answer: ThreadTest parallel analysis ────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- \texttt{ThreadTest}: Parallel Execution Analysis}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\textbf{Thread creation (one object, R2):}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException {
        ThreadTest obj = new ThreadTest(); // only ONE object (R2)

        Thread t1 = new Thread(() -> obj.f1(),        "T1");
        Thread t2 = new Thread(() -> obj.f2(),        "T2");
        Thread t3 = new Thread(() -> obj.f0(),        "T3");
        Thread t4 = new Thread(ThreadTest::fs1,       "T4");
        Thread t5 = new Thread(ThreadTest::fs2,       "T5");

        t1.start(); t2.start(); t3.start(); t4.start(); t5.start();
        t1.join();  t2.join();  t3.join();  t4.join();  t5.join();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{Lock analysis:}

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}llll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Thread} & \textbf{Method} & \textbf{Lock} & \textbf{Kind} \\
\midrule
T1 & \texttt{f1()} synchronized & \texttt{obj} (this) & instance \\
T2 & \texttt{f2()} synchronized & \texttt{obj} (this) & instance \\
T3 & \texttt{f0()} plain         & none               & --- \\
T4 & \texttt{fs1()} static sync  & \texttt{ThreadTest.class} & class \\
T5 & \texttt{fs2()} static sync  & \texttt{ThreadTest.class} & class \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip
\textbf{(i) Which threads run in parallel?}
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item \textbf{T3 runs in parallel with everyone.}
    \texttt{f0()} acquires no lock, so it never blocks and is never
    blocked by T1, T2, T4, or T5.
  \item \textbf{T1 or T2 runs in parallel with T4 or T5.}
    The instance lock (\texttt{obj}) and the class lock
    (\texttt{ThreadTest.class}) are \emph{different} objects, so
    an instance-method thread does not block a static-method thread
    and vice versa.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{(ii) Which threads do NOT run in parallel?}
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item \textbf{T1 and T2 cannot run in parallel} --- both compete
    for the instance lock \texttt{obj}; only one executes at a time.
  \item \textbf{T4 and T5 cannot run in parallel} --- both compete
    for the class lock \texttt{ThreadTest.class}.
\end{itemize}

\medskip
\textbf{Can R2 (\emph{only one object}) be relaxed?}

Yes.  If two separate instances \texttt{obj1} and \texttt{obj2} are
created, T1 (on \texttt{obj1}) and T2 (on \texttt{obj2}) acquire
\emph{different} instance locks and therefore \textbf{run in
parallel}.  Relaxing R2 increases concurrency between T1 and T2
without affecting the class-level synchronisation of T4 and T5.

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Describe two different ways of creating threads in Java. Which one is better and why? Explain the difference between a synchronized method and a synchronized statement. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2021--22}

%% ── Answer: Two ways + which is better + synchronization ────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer — Thread Creation, Preference \& Synchronization}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

Java provides two fundamental ways to create threads.

\medskip
\textbf{Way 1: Extending \texttt{Thread}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class CountThread extends Thread {
    public void run() {
        for (int i = 0; i < 5; i++)
            System.out.println(getName() + " -> " + i);
    }
}
// new CountThread().start();
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{Way 2: Implementing \texttt{Runnable}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class CountRunnable implements Runnable {
    public void run() {
        for (int i = 0; i < 5; i++)
            System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName() + " -> " + i);
    }
}
// new Thread(new CountRunnable()).start();
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{Which is better?}

Implementing \texttt{Runnable} is the preferred approach because:
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item Java supports only single inheritance; a class that already
    inherits from another class \emph{cannot} extend \texttt{Thread}.
    Implementing \texttt{Runnable} avoids this limitation.
  \item It cleanly separates task logic from thread management
    (separation of concerns).
  \item The same \texttt{Runnable} object can be reused across
    multiple threads or passed to an \texttt{ExecutorService}.
\end{itemize}

\medskip
\textcolor{cB}{\rule{\textwidth}{0.4pt}}
\medskip

\textbf{Synchronized method vs.\ synchronized statement}

A \textbf{synchronized method} places the lock on the entire method
body.  The implicit lock object is always \texttt{this}:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public synchronized void deposit(int amount) { balance += amount; }
\end{lstlisting}

A \textbf{synchronized statement} (block) locks only a specific section
of code and allows the programmer to choose the lock object explicitly,
enabling finer-grained concurrency:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public void deposit(int amount) {
    doSomeNonCriticalWork();   // runs without holding any lock
    synchronized (this) {
        balance += amount;     // only this block is mutually exclusive
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

Synchronized statements are preferred when only a small portion of
the method requires mutual exclusion, thereby reducing lock contention
and improving throughput.

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Find the minimum of a 1000-integer array using 5 threads in parallel:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class ParallelMin implements Runnable { /* your code */ }
class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        int[] numbers = new int[1000];
        ParallelMin[] parallelMin = new ParallelMin[5];
        // your code
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\mk{15}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2021--22}

%% ── Answer: ParallelMin skeleton completion ─────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Parallel Minimum of 1000-Element Array (5 Threads)}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

Each thread finds the minimum of its 200-element sub-array.
The main thread waits for all threads, then finds the global minimum
across the five partial results.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class ParallelMin implements Runnable {
    private final int[] numbers;
    private final int start, end;
    int localMin; // read by main after join()

    ParallelMin(int[] numbers, int start, int end) {
        this.numbers  = numbers;
        this.start    = start;
        this.end      = end;
        this.localMin = Integer.MAX_VALUE;
    }

    @Override
    public void run() {
        for (int i = start; i < end; i++)
            if (numbers[i] < localMin) localMin = numbers[i];
    }
}

class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException {
        int[] numbers = new int[1000];
        // Fill with sample data
        java.util.Random rnd = new java.util.Random();
        for (int i = 0; i < numbers.length; i++)
            numbers[i] = rnd.nextInt(10000);

        ParallelMin[] parallelMin = new ParallelMin[5];
        Thread[]      threads     = new Thread[5];
        int chunk = numbers.length / 5; // 200 each

        for (int i = 0; i < 5; i++) {
            parallelMin[i] = new ParallelMin(
                numbers, i * chunk, (i + 1) * chunk);
            threads[i] = new Thread(parallelMin[i]);
            threads[i].start();
        }
        for (Thread t : threads) t.join();

        int globalMin = Integer.MAX_VALUE;
        for (ParallelMin pm : parallelMin)
            if (pm.localMin < globalMin) globalMin = pm.localMin;

        System.out.println("Global minimum = " + globalMin);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item What are the two common ways to achieve synchronization between Threads? Which one gives more control? \mk{5}
\yr{CSE 107 | Jan 2021}

%% ── Answer: Two ways to achieve synchronisation ─────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer — Thread Synchronisation}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

The two common ways to achieve synchronisation in Java are:

\medskip
\textbf{1. Synchronized methods}

Add the \texttt{synchronized} keyword to a method declaration.  Java
automatically acquires the intrinsic lock (\textit{monitor}) of
\texttt{this} before executing the method body and releases it when
the method returns.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class Counter {
    private int count = 0;
    public synchronized void increment() { count++; }
    public synchronized int getCount()   { return count; }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{2. Synchronized statements (blocks)}

Wrap only the \emph{critical section} with \texttt{synchronized(obj)}
where \texttt{obj} is the object whose monitor you want to acquire.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class Counter {
    private int count = 0;
    private final Object lock = new Object();

    public void increment() {
        // non-critical work here (no lock held)
        synchronized (lock) {
            count++;          // only this line needs mutual exclusion
        }
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{Which gives more control?}

\textbf{Synchronized statements} give more control because:
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item The programmer can choose \emph{exactly which object} to lock
    on — it does not have to be \texttt{this}.
  \item The lock is held for the \emph{minimum necessary duration},
    reducing contention and improving concurrency.
  \item Multiple independent critical sections inside one class can
    use \emph{different} lock objects, allowing them to be entered
    concurrently by different threads.
\end{itemize}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Write complete Java code to compute the summation of 1 to 10{,}000 by dividing work equally among 5 different threads. Main thread waits and only prints the final summation. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2020--21}
\variant{CSE 201 | 2014--15}

%% ── Answer: Parallel summation with 5 threads ───────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer — Summation of 1 to 10{,}000 Using 5 Threads}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

The range $[1, 10000]$ is divided into 5 equal sub-ranges of 2000
numbers each.  Each thread computes the partial sum of its sub-range.
The main thread waits for all worker threads to finish via
\texttt{join()}, then sums the partial results and prints the total.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public class ParallelSum {

    static final int TOTAL   = 10000;
    static final int THREADS = 5;
    static final int RANGE   = TOTAL / THREADS;   // 2000 per thread

    // Array to store each thread's partial sum
    static long[] partialSum = new long[THREADS];

    static class SumTask implements Runnable {
        private final int id;     // thread index 0..4
        private final int start;  // inclusive
        private final int end;    // inclusive

        SumTask(int id, int start, int end) {
            this.id = id;
            this.start = start;
            this.end   = end;
        }

        @Override
        public void run() {
            long sum = 0;
            for (int i = start; i <= end; i++) sum += i;
            partialSum[id] = sum;
            System.out.println("Thread-" + id +
                " summed [" + start + ", " + end + "] = " + sum);
        }
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException {
        Thread[] workers = new Thread[THREADS];

        // Create and start each worker
        for (int i = 0; i < THREADS; i++) {
            int start = i * RANGE + 1;
            int end   = start + RANGE - 1;
            workers[i] = new Thread(new SumTask(i, start, end));
            workers[i].start();
        }

        // Main thread waits for all workers
        for (Thread t : workers) t.join();

        // Aggregate partial sums
        long total = 0;
        for (long ps : partialSum) total += ps;

        System.out.println("\nFinal Summation (1 to 10000) = " + total);
        // Expected: 50_050_000
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{How work is divided:}

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}clcc@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Thread} & \textbf{Range} & \textbf{Partial Sum} \\
\midrule
Thread-0 & 1 -- 2000    & 2{,}001{,}000 \\
Thread-1 & 2001 -- 4000 & 6{,}001{,}000 \\
Thread-2 & 4001 -- 6000 & 10{,}001{,}000 \\
Thread-3 & 6001 -- 8000 & 14{,}001{,}000 \\
Thread-4 & 8001 -- 10000 & 18{,}045{,}000 \\
\midrule
\textbf{Total} & & \textbf{50{,}050{,}000} \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

Note: \texttt{partialSum} is written by each thread to a
\emph{distinct index}, so no synchronisation is needed for the write.
The main thread reads only after all \texttt{join()} calls complete,
ensuring full visibility.

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Write Java code to compute the summation of 1 to 10{,}000{,}000 by dividing the work equally among 10 threads (no formula allowed, only loops). The main thread waits for all threads to finish and prints the final summation. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | Jan 2021}

%% ── Answer: Sum 1..10,000,000 loops only ────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Sum 1 to 10{,}000{,}000 (10 Threads, Loops Only)}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public class SumLoop10M {

    static final int TOTAL   = 10000000;
    static final int THREADS = 10;
    static final int CHUNK   = TOTAL / THREADS; // 1,000,000

    static long[] partial = new long[THREADS];

    static class SumTask implements Runnable {
        private final int id, start, end;
        SumTask(int id, int start, int end) {
            this.id = id; this.start = start; this.end = end;
        }
        @Override
        public void run() {
            long sum = 0;
            for (int i = start; i <= end; i++) // loop only, no formula
                sum += i;
            partial[id] = sum;
        }
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException {
        Thread[] threads = new Thread[THREADS];
        for (int i = 0; i < THREADS; i++) {
            int s = i * CHUNK + 1;
            int e = s + CHUNK - 1;
            threads[i] = new Thread(new SumTask(i, s, e));
            threads[i].start();
        }
        for (Thread t : threads) t.join(); // main waits

        long total = 0;
        for (long p : partial) total += p;
        System.out.println("Final sum = " + total);
        // Expected: 50,000,005,000,000
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Write Java code to compute the summation of 1 to 10{,}000 by dividing the work equally among 5 threads (no formula allowed, only loops). The main thread waits for all threads to finish and prints the final summation. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2020--21}

%% ── Answer: Sum 1..10,000 with 5 threads, loops only ───────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Sum 1 to 10{,}000 (5 Threads, Loops Only)}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public class SumLoop10K {

    static final int TOTAL   = 10000;
    static final int THREADS = 5;
    static final int CHUNK   = TOTAL / THREADS; // 2000 each

    static long[] partial = new long[THREADS];

    static class SumTask implements Runnable {
        private final int id, start, end;
        SumTask(int id, int start, int end) {
            this.id = id; this.start = start; this.end = end;
        }
        @Override
        public void run() {
            long sum = 0;
            for (int i = start; i <= end; i++) sum += i;
            partial[id] = sum;
        }
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException {
        Thread[] threads = new Thread[THREADS];
        for (int i = 0; i < THREADS; i++) {
            int s = i * CHUNK + 1;
            int e = s + CHUNK - 1;
            threads[i] = new Thread(new SumTask(i, s, e));
            threads[i].start();
        }
        for (Thread t : threads) t.join();

        long total = 0;
        for (long p : partial) total += p;
        System.out.println("Final sum = " + total); // 50,005,000
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Consider the Producer-Consumer problem with buffer of size 1. The producer generates letters A--Z circularly. The reader reads and displays them. Use wait/notifyAll or \texttt{ArrayBlockingQueue}. \mk{15}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2019--20, Jan 2021}
\variant{CSE 201 | 2013--14}

%% ── Answer: Producer-Consumer A-Z circular ─────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Producer-Consumer: A--Z Circular, Buffer Size 1}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\textbf{Solution 1 --- Using \texttt{wait} / \texttt{notifyAll}}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class Buffer {
    private char data;
    private boolean hasData = false;

    public synchronized void put(char c) throws InterruptedException {
        while (hasData) wait();       // wait if buffer is full
        data = c;
        hasData = true;
        System.out.println("Produced: " + c);
        notifyAll();
    }

    public synchronized char get() throws InterruptedException {
        while (!hasData) wait();      // wait if buffer is empty
        hasData = false;
        System.out.println("Consumed: " + data);
        notifyAll();
        return data;
    }
}

class Producer extends Thread {
    private final Buffer buf;
    Producer(Buffer buf) { this.buf = buf; }
    @Override
    public void run() {
        try {
            for (int cycle = 0; cycle < 2; cycle++) // 2 full cycles
                for (char c = 'A'; c <= 'Z'; c++)
                    buf.put(c);
        } catch (InterruptedException e) { e.printStackTrace(); }
    }
}

class Consumer extends Thread {
    private final Buffer buf;
    Consumer(Buffer buf) { this.buf = buf; }
    @Override
    public void run() {
        try {
            for (int i = 0; i < 52; i++) // 2 x 26 letters
                buf.get();
        } catch (InterruptedException e) { e.printStackTrace(); }
    }
}

public class ProducerConsumerAZ {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Buffer buf = new Buffer();
        new Producer(buf).start();
        new Consumer(buf).start();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{Solution 2 --- Using \texttt{ArrayBlockingQueue} (simpler)}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.concurrent.ArrayBlockingQueue;

public class ProducerConsumerAZBQ {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        ArrayBlockingQueue<Character> queue =
            new ArrayBlockingQueue<>(1);

        Thread producer = new Thread(() -> {
            try {
                for (int cycle = 0; cycle < 2; cycle++)
                    for (char c = 'A'; c <= 'Z'; c++) {
                        queue.put(c);
                        System.out.println("Produced: " + c);
                    }
            } catch (InterruptedException e) {}
        });

        Thread consumer = new Thread(() -> {
            try {
                for (int i = 0; i < 52; i++) {
                    char c = queue.take();
                    System.out.println("Consumed: " + c);
                }
            } catch (InterruptedException e) {}
        });

        producer.start();
        consumer.start();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Mr. Chandler and Ms. Phoebe worked in the same place. Their work is to put and get
product in a shared inventory array of size 3. Ms. Phoebe puts a single product in the
inventory and Mr. Chandler gets a single product from the inventory at a time. Ms.
Phoebe cannot put a product to the inventory if the inventory array is full with 4
products. Mr. Chandler cannot get a product from a inventory if the inventory array
contains no product. Ms. Phoebe can put a product to the inventory if any one of the
place of the inventory array is empty. Mr. Chandler can get a product from the inventory
if any one of the place of the inventory array is full with a product. Write a java code to
solve the above mentioned problem using the concepts of inter thread communication.
You can use \textbf{wait/notifyAll} or \textbf{ArrayBlockingQueue}. \mk{10}\yr{CSE 107 | Jan 2021, 2019--20}
\variant{CSE 201 | 2014--15, 2008--09, 2009--10}

%% ── Answer: Chandler-Phoebe inventory (both solutions) ─────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Chandler \& Phoebe: Shared Inventory of Size 3}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\textbf{Solution 1 --- Using \texttt{wait} / \texttt{notifyAll}}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class Inventory {
    private final int[] slots;
    private int count = 0;

    Inventory(int size) { slots = new int[size]; }

    public synchronized void put(int product)
            throws InterruptedException {
        while (count == slots.length) wait(); // full -- Phoebe waits
        slots[count++] = product;
        System.out.println("Phoebe put product " + product
                           + "  [count=" + count + "]");
        notifyAll();
    }

    public synchronized int get() throws InterruptedException {
        while (count == 0) wait(); // empty -- Chandler waits
        int product = slots[--count];
        System.out.println("Chandler got product " + product
                           + "  [count=" + count + "]");
        notifyAll();
        return product;
    }
}

class Phoebe extends Thread {
    private final Inventory inv;
    Phoebe(Inventory inv) { this.inv = inv; }
    @Override
    public void run() {
        try {
            for (int i = 1; i <= 10; i++) inv.put(i);
        } catch (InterruptedException e) {}
    }
}

class Chandler extends Thread {
    private final Inventory inv;
    Chandler(Inventory inv) { this.inv = inv; }
    @Override
    public void run() {
        try {
            for (int i = 0; i < 10; i++) inv.get();
        } catch (InterruptedException e) {}
    }
}

public class InventoryDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Inventory inv = new Inventory(3);
        new Phoebe(inv).start();
        new Chandler(inv).start();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{Solution 2 --- Using \texttt{ArrayBlockingQueue}}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.concurrent.ArrayBlockingQueue;

public class InventoryBQ {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        ArrayBlockingQueue<Integer> inv = new ArrayBlockingQueue<>(3);

        Thread phoebe = new Thread(() -> {
            try {
                for (int i = 1; i <= 10; i++) {
                    inv.put(i);
                    System.out.println("Phoebe put " + i);
                }
            } catch (InterruptedException e) {}
        });

        Thread chandler = new Thread(() -> {
            try {
                for (int i = 0; i < 10; i++) {
                    int p = inv.take();
                    System.out.println("Chandler got " + p);
                }
            } catch (InterruptedException e) {}
        });

        phoebe.start();
        chandler.start();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}


\item Mr. P puts products and Mr. C gets products from a shared inventory of size 4. P cannot put if full (4 products); C cannot get if empty. Write complete Java code using \textbf{wait and notifyAll only} --- you are not allowed to use \texttt{BlockingQueue}. \mk{20}
\yr{CSE 107 | Jan 2021}

%% ── Answer: P/C inventory, wait/notifyAll only ──────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Mr.\ P \& Mr.\ C: Inventory Size 4, \texttt{wait}/\texttt{notifyAll} Only}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\texttt{BlockingQueue} is \textbf{not} used.  All synchronisation is
implemented with Java's built-in monitor (\texttt{synchronized} +
\texttt{wait} + \texttt{notifyAll}).

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class SharedInventory {
    private final int MAX = 4;
    private final int[] slots = new int[MAX];
    private int count = 0;

    // Called by P (Producer)
    public synchronized void put(int item)
            throws InterruptedException {
        while (count == MAX) {      // inventory full -- P waits
            System.out.println("P waiting (inventory full)");
            wait();
        }
        slots[count++] = item;
        System.out.println("P put item " + item
                           + "  [size=" + count + "]");
        notifyAll();                // wake C if it was waiting
    }

    // Called by C (Consumer)
    public synchronized int get() throws InterruptedException {
        while (count == 0) {       // inventory empty -- C waits
            System.out.println("C waiting (inventory empty)");
            wait();
        }
        int item = slots[--count];
        System.out.println("C got item " + item
                           + "  [size=" + count + "]");
        notifyAll();               // wake P if it was waiting
        return item;
    }
}

class Producer extends Thread {
    private final SharedInventory inv;
    Producer(SharedInventory inv) { this.inv = inv; }
    @Override
    public void run() {
        try {
            for (int i = 1; i <= 12; i++) {
                inv.put(i);
                Thread.sleep(50); // simulate production time
            }
        } catch (InterruptedException e) {}
    }
}

class Consumer extends Thread {
    private final SharedInventory inv;
    Consumer(SharedInventory inv) { this.inv = inv; }
    @Override
    public void run() {
        try {
            for (int i = 0; i < 12; i++) {
                inv.get();
                Thread.sleep(150); // simulate consumption time
            }
        } catch (InterruptedException e) {}
    }
}

public class InventoryWaitNotify {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        SharedInventory inv = new SharedInventory();
        new Producer(inv).start();
        new Consumer(inv).start();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Key points:}
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item \texttt{while} (not \texttt{if}) guards each \texttt{wait()}
    to handle spurious wake-ups correctly.
  \item \texttt{notifyAll()} is used instead of \texttt{notify()} to
    avoid the risk of notifying the wrong thread.
  \item Both \texttt{put} and \texttt{get} are \texttt{synchronized}
    on the same object (\texttt{inv}), so only one thread executes
    either method at a time.
\end{itemize}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Consider the \texttt{TestClass} with \texttt{f1()} (1s sleep) and \texttt{f2()} (2s sleep). Create two threads without changing \texttt{TestClass} or extending/implementing any class:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class TestClass {
    public void f1() { for(int i=0;i<5;i++) { System.out.println(i); try { Thread.sleep(1000); } catch(InterruptedException e){} } }
    public static void f2() { for(int i=0;i<5;i++) { System.out.println(i); try { Thread.sleep(2000); } catch(InterruptedException e){} } }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | Jan 2021}

%% ── Answer: Lambda threads for f1 and f2 ────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Two Threads via Lambda (No Subclassing)}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

Because we cannot extend or implement any class, we use
\textbf{lambda expressions} as \texttt{Runnable} instances.
\texttt{TestClass} is used as-is; a single object is created for the
instance method \texttt{f1()}, while the static method \texttt{f2()}
is referenced directly.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException {
        TestClass obj = new TestClass();

        // Thread for f1() -- instance method, needs an object
        Thread t1 = new Thread(() -> obj.f1(), "T1");

        // Thread for f2() -- static method, no object needed
        Thread t2 = new Thread(TestClass::f2, "T2");

        t1.start();
        t2.start();

        t1.join();
        t2.join();

        System.out.println("Both threads finished.");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Why this satisfies all constraints:}
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item \texttt{TestClass} is not modified.
  \item No new class extends or implements anything ---
    \texttt{() -> obj.f1()} is an anonymous lambda that the compiler
    treats as a \texttt{Runnable} without requiring an explicit
    \texttt{implements Runnable} declaration.
  \item Two separate threads (\texttt{t1} for \texttt{f1()},
    \texttt{t2} for \texttt{f2()}) are created and run concurrently.
\end{itemize}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Explain with code how to fix the \texttt{SharedCounter} class so that multiple threads can correctly operate on it:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class SharedCounter {
    private int counter;
    SharedCounter() { this.counter = 0; }
    private void increment() { this.counter++; }
    public int get() { return this.counter; }
    public void count() { for(int i=1;i<=1000;i++) increment(); }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\mk{5}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2020--21}

%% ── Answer: Fix SharedCounter ───────────────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Fixing \texttt{SharedCounter} for Thread Safety}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\textbf{The problem:}

\texttt{counter++} is \emph{not atomic} --- it compiles to three
operations: read, increment, write.  Two threads can both read the
same value, both increment it, and both write back, losing one
update (a \emph{lost update} race condition).

\medskip
\textbf{Fix --- make \texttt{increment()} synchronized:}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class SharedCounter {
    private int counter;
    SharedCounter() { this.counter = 0; }

    // Fix: add synchronized so only one thread increments at a time
    private synchronized void increment() { this.counter++; }

    public int get() { return this.counter; }

    public void count() {
        for (int i = 1; i <= 1000; i++) increment();
    }
}

public class TestSharedCounter {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException {
        SharedCounter sc = new SharedCounter();

        Thread t1 = new Thread(sc::count, "T1");
        Thread t2 = new Thread(sc::count, "T2");
        Thread t3 = new Thread(sc::count, "T3");

        t1.start(); t2.start(); t3.start();
        t1.join();  t2.join();  t3.join();

        System.out.println("Final count: " + sc.get()); // always 3000
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Alternative fix --- use \texttt{AtomicInteger}:}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.concurrent.atomic.AtomicInteger;

class SharedCounterAtomic {
    private AtomicInteger counter = new AtomicInteger(0);
    private void increment()  { counter.incrementAndGet(); }
    public  int  get()        { return counter.get(); }
    public  void count()      { for (int i=1;i<=1000;i++) increment(); }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\texttt{AtomicInteger.incrementAndGet()} is a single hardware-level
atomic operation and avoids the overhead of acquiring a monitor lock.

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Write three different ways to create Threads in Java with short code examples. What is the difference between synchronized method and synchronized statement? \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2019--20}

%% ── Answer: Three ways to create threads + synchronization ──────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
