  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer — Three Ways to Create Threads \& Synchronization}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\textbf{Way 1: Extending \texttt{Thread}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class T1 extends Thread {
    public void run() { System.out.println("Thread via extension"); }
}
// Usage: new T1().start();
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{Way 2: Implementing \texttt{Runnable}}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class T2 implements Runnable {
    public void run() { System.out.println("Thread via Runnable"); }
}
// Usage: new Thread(new T2()).start();
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{Way 3: Using a Lambda expression (Java 8+)}

Since \texttt{Runnable} is a functional interface, it can be expressed
as a lambda — the most concise modern approach.
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
Thread t = new Thread(() -> System.out.println("Thread via Lambda"));
t.start();
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textcolor{cB}{\rule{\textwidth}{0.4pt}}
\medskip

\textbf{Synchronized method vs.\ synchronized statement}

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{@{}p{0.44\linewidth}p{0.44\linewidth}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Synchronized Method} & \textbf{Synchronized Statement (Block)} \\
\midrule
The \texttt{synchronized} keyword is placed in the method signature.
The lock acquired is always \texttt{this} (or the \texttt{Class} object
for \texttt{static} methods). &
The \texttt{synchronized} keyword wraps only a \emph{critical section}
inside a method, and the programmer specifies \emph{which object} to
lock on. \\[6pt]
Entire method body is mutually exclusive. &
Only the enclosed block is mutually exclusive; the rest of the method
runs without holding the lock. \\[6pt]
Less flexible — always locks the current object. &
More flexible — can lock on any object, enabling finer-grained
concurrency. \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// Synchronized method
public synchronized void increment() {
    count++;
}

// Synchronized statement -- locks only on the shared 'counter' object
public void increment() {
    // ... non-critical code runs here without holding a lock ...
    synchronized (counter) {
        count++;
    }
    // ... more non-critical code ...
}
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Divide summation of 1 to 10{,}000{,}000 equally among 10 different threads. Main thread waits and prints final sum. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2019--20}

%% ── Answer: Sum 1..10,000,000 with 10 threads ──────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Summation of 1 to 10{,}000{,}000 Using 10 Threads}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

The range $[1,\,10{,}000{,}000]$ is divided into 10 equal sub-ranges
of 1{,}000{,}000 numbers each.  Each thread computes its partial sum
and stores it in a shared array.  The main thread calls
\texttt{join()} on every worker before aggregating the results.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public class ParallelSum {

    static final int TOTAL   = 10000000;
    static final int THREADS = 10;
    static final int RANGE   = TOTAL / THREADS; // 1,000,000 each

    static long[] partial = new long[THREADS];

    static class SumTask implements Runnable {
        private final int id, start, end;
        SumTask(int id, int start, int end) {
            this.id = id; this.start = start; this.end = end;
        }
        @Override
        public void run() {
            long sum = 0;
            for (int i = start; i <= end; i++) sum += i;
            partial[id] = sum;
        }
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException {
        Thread[] workers = new Thread[THREADS];
        for (int i = 0; i < THREADS; i++) {
            int s = i * RANGE + 1;
            int e = s + RANGE - 1;
            workers[i] = new Thread(new SumTask(i, s, e));
            workers[i].start();
        }
        for (Thread t : workers) t.join(); // main waits

        long total = 0;
        for (long p : partial) total += p;
        System.out.println("Sum = " + total); // 50,000,005,000,000
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item What are the advantages of multithreading over process-based multitasking? \mk{6}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2017--18; CSE 201 | 2012--13}

%% ── Answer: Multithreading vs process-based multitasking ────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer — Multithreading vs.\ Process-Based Multitasking}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\textbf{Process-based multitasking} (multiprocessing) runs multiple
independent programs concurrently; each process has its own address
space and system resources.  \textbf{Thread-based multitasking}
(multithreading) runs multiple threads \emph{within the same process},
all sharing the same memory and resources.

\medskip
\textbf{Advantages of multithreading over process-based multitasking:}

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textbf{\arabic*.}]
  \item \textbf{Lower overhead:} Creating a thread is far cheaper than
    creating a process because threads share the heap, code segment,
    and open file descriptors of their parent process.  No new virtual
    address space needs to be set up.

  \item \textbf{Faster context switching:} Switching between threads
    of the same process is faster than switching between processes
    because the operating system does not need to swap the entire
    memory map — only the CPU registers and stack pointer change.

  \item \textbf{Shared memory — easier communication:} Threads in the
    same process share the same address space, so data can be
    exchanged through shared variables without expensive inter-process
    communication (IPC) mechanisms such as pipes, sockets, or shared
    memory segments.

  \item \textbf{Responsiveness:} In a multithreaded GUI application,
    one thread can handle user interaction while another performs a
    long computation, keeping the application responsive.

  \item \textbf{Better CPU utilisation:} When one thread is blocked on
    I/O, the CPU can execute another thread of the same process,
    improving throughput without spawning new heavy-weight processes.

  \item \textbf{Simplified program structure:} Tasks that are
    naturally concurrent (e.g.\ reading input and writing output
    simultaneously) can be modelled as separate threads within a
    single program, rather than as separate communicating processes.
\end{enumerate}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Describe the methods Java uses for inter-thread communication. \mk{9}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2017--18}

%% ── Answer: Inter-thread communication ──────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer — Inter-Thread Communication in Java}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

Java's inter-thread communication is built on three methods defined
in the \texttt{Object} class.  Because every object has a monitor,
these methods can be called on \emph{any} object; however, they must
always be called from within a \texttt{synchronized} block or method
(otherwise Java throws \texttt{IllegalMonitorStateException}).

\medskip
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}p{0.22\linewidth}p{0.68\linewidth}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Method} & \textbf{Description} \\
\midrule
\texttt{wait()} &
  Causes the current thread to release the monitor lock and enter the
  \emph{Waiting} state.  The thread remains waiting until another
  thread calls \texttt{notify()} or \texttt{notifyAll()} on the same
  object, or until it is interrupted. \\[4pt]
\texttt{notify()} &
  Wakes up \emph{one} arbitrary thread that is waiting on this object's
  monitor.  The awakened thread must re-acquire the lock before it can
  proceed. \\[4pt]
\texttt{notifyAll()} &
  Wakes up \emph{all} threads waiting on this object's monitor.  All
  awakened threads compete to reacquire the lock; only one succeeds at
  a time. \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip
\textbf{Classic Producer–Consumer example:}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class SharedBuffer {
    private int data;
    private boolean hasData = false;

    // Called by Producer thread
    public synchronized void produce(int val) throws InterruptedException {
        while (hasData)         // wait if buffer is full
            wait();
        data = val;
        hasData = true;
        System.out.println("Produced: " + val);
        notify();               // wake up Consumer
    }

    // Called by Consumer thread
    public synchronized int consume() throws InterruptedException {
        while (!hasData)        // wait if buffer is empty
            wait();
        hasData = false;
        System.out.println("Consumed: " + data);
        notify();               // wake up Producer
        return data;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Key rules:}
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item Always call \texttt{wait()} inside a \texttt{while} loop (not
    \texttt{if}), because of \emph{spurious wake-ups} — a thread may
    wake up even without a \texttt{notify()}.
  \item Prefer \texttt{notifyAll()} over \texttt{notify()} when
    multiple threads may be waiting, to avoid potential deadlock from
    notifying the wrong thread.
\end{itemize}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item What are the two ways of creating a thread? Give an example for each kind. Which one is better and why? \mk{8+5}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2011--12; CSE 107 | 2016--17}
\variant{CSE 201 | 2009--10, 2012--13}

%% ── Answer: Two ways to create a thread ─────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer — Two Ways to Create a Thread in Java}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

Java provides two mechanisms to create a thread.

\medskip
\textbf{Way 1: Extending the \texttt{Thread} class}

Create a subclass of \texttt{Thread} and override its \texttt{run()} method.
The thread is started by calling \texttt{start()} on an instance of the subclass.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class MyThread extends Thread {
    private String name;
    MyThread(String name) { this.name = name; }

    @Override
    public void run() {
        for (int i = 1; i <= 3; i++) {
            System.out.println(name + " - count: " + i);
        }
    }
}

public class ThreadDemo1 {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException {
        MyThread t1 = new MyThread("Thread-A");
        MyThread t2 = new MyThread("Thread-B");
        t1.start();
        t2.start();
        t1.join();   // main waits for t1 to finish
        t2.join();   // main waits for t2 to finish
        System.out.println("Main thread ends.");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{Way 2: Implementing the \texttt{Runnable} interface}

Implement the \texttt{Runnable} interface and pass an instance of it
to a \texttt{Thread} object.  The class is free to extend any other
class simultaneously.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class MyRunnable implements Runnable {
    private String name;
    MyRunnable(String name) { this.name = name; }

    @Override
    public void run() {
        for (int i = 1; i <= 3; i++) {
            System.out.println(name + " - count: " + i);
        }
    }
}

public class ThreadDemo2 {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException {
        Thread t1 = new Thread(new MyRunnable("Thread-A"));
        Thread t2 = new Thread(new MyRunnable("Thread-B"));
        t1.start();
        t2.start();
        t1.join();
        t2.join();
        System.out.println("Main thread ends.");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{Which is better and why?}

Implementing \texttt{Runnable} is \emph{generally preferred} for the
following reasons:

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textbf{\arabic*.}]
  \item \textbf{Single Inheritance constraint:} Java does not support
    multiple inheritance.  If a class already extends another class,
    it \emph{cannot} also extend \texttt{Thread}.  Implementing
    \texttt{Runnable} imposes no such restriction.
  \item \textbf{Separation of concerns:} \texttt{Runnable} separates
    the task logic from the thread mechanism, making code more modular
    and reusable.
  \item \textbf{Resource efficiency:} The same \texttt{Runnable}
    object can be submitted to thread pools (e.g.\
    \texttt{ExecutorService}), whereas a \texttt{Thread} subclass
    cannot be reused after termination.
  \item \textbf{Better OOP design:} Extending \texttt{Thread} is
    appropriate only when you need to modify the threading behaviour
    itself, which is rarely required in practice.
\end{enumerate}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Find the minimum of a 500-integer array using 5 threads in parallel. You are not allowed to write any more classes or arrays, but you can add normal variables, constructors, and other methods:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class ParallelMin implements Runnable { /* your code */ }
class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Random random = new Random();
        int[] numbers = new int[500];
        for (int i = 0; i < numbers.length; i++)
            numbers[i] = random.nextInt();
        // your code
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2016--17}

%% ── Answer: ParallelMin 500 elements, no extra classes/arrays ───────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Parallel Minimum of 500-Element Array (No Extra Arrays)}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

The constraint forbids additional classes or arrays.  The partial
minimum of each thread is stored as an instance field of
\texttt{ParallelMin} and accessed directly through the object
reference after \texttt{join()}.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class ParallelMin implements Runnable {
    private final int[] numbers;
    private final int start, end;
    int localMin;

    ParallelMin(int[] numbers, int start, int end) {
        this.numbers  = numbers;
        this.start    = start;
        this.end      = end;
        this.localMin = Integer.MAX_VALUE;
    }

    @Override
    public void run() {
        for (int i = start; i < end; i++)
            if (numbers[i] < localMin) localMin = numbers[i];
    }
}

class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException {
        Random random = new Random();
        int[] numbers = new int[500];
        for (int i = 0; i < numbers.length; i++)
            numbers[i] = random.nextInt();

        // 5 objects hold the partial results -- no extra array needed
        int chunk = numbers.length / 5; // 100 each
        ParallelMin pm0 = new ParallelMin(numbers,   0, 100);
        ParallelMin pm1 = new ParallelMin(numbers, 100, 200);
        ParallelMin pm2 = new ParallelMin(numbers, 200, 300);
        ParallelMin pm3 = new ParallelMin(numbers, 300, 400);
        ParallelMin pm4 = new ParallelMin(numbers, 400, 500);

        Thread t0=new Thread(pm0), t1=new Thread(pm1),
               t2=new Thread(pm2), t3=new Thread(pm3),
               t4=new Thread(pm4);

        t0.start(); t1.start(); t2.start(); t3.start(); t4.start();
        t0.join();  t1.join();  t2.join();  t3.join();  t4.join();

        int globalMin = Math.min(pm0.localMin,
                        Math.min(pm1.localMin,
                        Math.min(pm2.localMin,
                        Math.min(pm3.localMin, pm4.localMin))));

        System.out.println("Global minimum = " + globalMin);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item You need to simulate the traffic behavior of different vehicles moving inside BUET
campus. There are four types, i.e., Car, Microbus, AutoRickshaw, and Rickshaw, of
vehicles run in the campus. Each vehicle type should have necessary properties, e.g.,
number of wheels, maximum speed, etc., which represent real vehicles that you see in
real life. In the simulated environment you need to instantiate 10 vehicles of each type,
where each vehicle has its current position and speed. Their initial positions and speeds
will be randomly generated while you instantiate these vehicles. Vehicles will run along
the road segments which are represented as a fixed set of rectangles. In every second,
each vehicle updates its position based on the previous position and current speed. You
need to make sure that a vehicle does not go outside the road segments at any point of
time. Two vehicles must not collide with each other, i.e., if during a position update a
vehicle finds another vehicle within a threshold range it cannot move and must need to
decrease its speed.

Write a Java program to implement the above simulator. You have to run each vehicle
as a thread. Please make your own assumption to build the whole scenario as realistic as
possible to reflect the real-world scenario. \mk{35}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2015--16}

%% ── Answer: BUET Traffic Simulation ────────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- BUET Campus Traffic Simulation}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

Each vehicle type is a subclass of an abstract \texttt{Vehicle} thread and
carries type-specific properties (number of wheels, maximum speed).
Initial positions and speeds are randomly generated.
A shared \texttt{Road} object serialises position updates: if another
vehicle is found within a configurable \emph{threshold} range the vehicle
stays put and its speed is decreased; if the road boundary would be
exceeded the vehicle is clamped to the boundary.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.Random;

// -- Shared road segment ------------------------------------------
class Road {
    static final int LENGTH    = 500;  // road length in metres
    static final int THRESHOLD = 10;   // collision-detection range

    // Coarse-grained lock: one position-update at a time
    public synchronized int tryMove(int oldPos, int newPos,
                                    int[] allPositions, int myIdx) {
        // 1. Clamp to road boundaries
        newPos = Math.max(0, Math.min(LENGTH - 1, newPos));

        // 2. Check threshold range against every other vehicle
        for (int i = 0; i < allPositions.length; i++) {
            if (i == myIdx) continue;
            if (Math.abs(allPositions[i] - newPos) < THRESHOLD)
                return -1;   // blocked — caller must decrease speed
        }
        return newPos;
    }
}

// -- Abstract vehicle thread --------------------------------------
abstract class Vehicle extends Thread {
    protected int    position;
    protected int    speed;            // metres per second
    protected final int    maxSpeed;
    protected final int    numWheels;
    protected final Road   road;
    protected final int[]  allPositions;  // shared position array
    protected final int    myIdx;
    private   static final Random rng = new Random();

    Vehicle(String name, int maxSpeed, int numWheels,
            Road road, int[] allPositions, int idx) {
        super(name);
        this.maxSpeed     = maxSpeed;
        this.numWheels    = numWheels;
        this.road         = road;
        this.allPositions = allPositions;
        this.myIdx        = idx;
        // Random initial position and speed
        this.position     = rng.nextInt(Road.LENGTH);
        this.speed        = 1 + rng.nextInt(maxSpeed);
        allPositions[idx] = this.position;
    }

    @Override
    public void run() {
        try {
            for (int step = 0; step < 30; step++) {
                int next   = position + speed;
                int result = road.tryMove(position, next,
                                          allPositions, myIdx);
                if (result == -1) {
                    // Blocked by nearby vehicle: decrease speed
                    speed = Math.max(1, speed - 1);
                    System.out.printf("%-22s BLOCKED  pos=%d speed->%d%n",
                                      getName(), position, speed);
                } else {
                    position = result;
                    allPositions[myIdx] = position;
                    // Gradually recover speed up to maximum
                    if (speed < maxSpeed) speed++;
                    System.out.printf("%-22s pos=%d speed=%d%n",
                                      getName(), position, speed);
                }
                Thread.sleep(1000); // update every second
            }
        } catch (InterruptedException e) {
            Thread.currentThread().interrupt();
        }
    }
}

// -- Concrete vehicle types (wheels, max speed are assumptions) ---
class Car extends Vehicle {
    // 4 wheels, max speed 60 m/s (assumed scaled for simulation)
    Car(Road r, int[] pos, int idx) {
        super("Car-" + idx, 60, 4, r, pos, idx);
    }
}
class Microbus extends Vehicle {
    // 4 wheels, max speed 40 m/s
    Microbus(Road r, int[] pos, int idx) {
        super("Microbus-" + idx, 40, 4, r, pos, idx);
    }
}
class AutoRickshaw extends Vehicle {
    // 3 wheels, max speed 25 m/s
    AutoRickshaw(Road r, int[] pos, int idx) {
        super("AutoRickshaw-" + idx, 25, 3, r, pos, idx);
    }
}
class Rickshaw extends Vehicle {
    // 3 wheels, max speed 10 m/s
    Rickshaw(Road r, int[] pos, int idx) {
        super("Rickshaw-" + idx, 10, 3, r, pos, idx);
    }
}

// -- Main ---------------------------------------------------------
public class BUETTraffic {
    static final int PER_TYPE = 10;
    static final int TOTAL    = PER_TYPE * 4;   // 40 vehicles

    public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException {
        Road  road        = new Road();
        int[] allPositions = new int[TOTAL];
        Vehicle[] vehicles = new Vehicle[TOTAL];

        int idx = 0;
        for (int i = 0; i < PER_TYPE; i++)
            vehicles[idx] = new Car(road, allPositions, idx++);
        for (int i = 0; i < PER_TYPE; i++)
            vehicles[idx] = new Microbus(road, allPositions, idx++);
        for (int i = 0; i < PER_TYPE; i++)
            vehicles[idx] = new AutoRickshaw(road, allPositions, idx++);
        for (int i = 0; i < PER_TYPE; i++)
            vehicles[idx] = new Rickshaw(road, allPositions, idx++);

        for (Vehicle v : vehicles) v.start();
        for (Vehicle v : vehicles) v.join();

        System.out.println("Simulation complete.");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Key design decisions and guarantees:}
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item \textbf{Vehicle properties:} Each subclass fixes
    \texttt{numWheels} and \texttt{maxSpeed} to realistic values
    (Car: 4 wheels / 60; Microbus: 4 / 40; AutoRickshaw: 3 / 25;
    Rickshaw: 3 / 10).
  \item \textbf{Random initialisation:} Both \texttt{position} and
    \texttt{speed} are drawn from a uniform random distribution at
    construction time, satisfying the problem statement.
  \item \textbf{Boundary enforcement:} \texttt{Math.max/min} clamps
    \texttt{newPos} to $[0, \texttt{LENGTH}-1]$ so no vehicle ever
    leaves the road segment.
  \item \textbf{Threshold-based collision:} \texttt{tryMove()} scans
    all other vehicles; if any is within \texttt{THRESHOLD} cells of
    the intended new position the move is refused and the caller
    decrements its speed by 1 (minimum 1), matching the specification
    exactly.
  \item \textbf{Thread safety:} \texttt{tryMove()} is
    \texttt{synchronized} on the \texttt{Road} object, so the shared
    \texttt{allPositions[]} array is read and written atomically,
    preventing race conditions.
  \item \textbf{Periodic update:} Each vehicle calls
    \texttt{Thread.sleep(1000)} between steps, implementing the
    ``every second'' update cycle required by the problem.
\end{itemize}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Why are \texttt{suspend()}, \texttt{resume()} and \texttt{stop()} methods of \texttt{Thread} class deprecated? Demonstrate how you can achieve suspend, resume and stop behaviors in a thread that you have implemented, without using the deprecated methods. Write necessary code and provide explanations where appropriate. Do not use unnecessary/redundant \texttt{sleep}, \texttt{wait} or \texttt{notify} method calls. \mk{5+10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2015--16}

%% ── Answer: Deprecated thread methods ───────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Deprecated Thread Methods and Safe Implementation}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\textbf{Why These Methods Are Deprecated:}
\begin{enumerate}
    \item \textbf{\texttt{stop()}:} It is inherently unsafe. It stops a thread abruptly by throwing a \texttt{ThreadDeath} exception up the stack, causing the thread to instantly release all locks/monitors it holds. If any shared objects protected by those locks were in an incomplete or transitioning state, they are exposed to other threads in a corrupted, inconsistent state.
    \item \textbf{\texttt{suspend()} / \texttt{resume()}:} They are inherently deadlock-prone. When a thread is frozen via \texttt{suspend()}, it does \textbf{not} release any locks it currently holds. If the managing thread trying to call \texttt{resume()} requires access to any of those same locked resources before it can proceed, the application reaches an unrecoverable deadlock.
\end{enumerate}

\medskip
\textbf{Safe Design Pattern:}
To accurately replace these behaviors without creating redundant or resource-heavy busy-waiting loops, state flags (\texttt{active} and \texttt{paused}) are declared as \texttt{volatile} to ensure visibility across threads. Inter-thread communication primitives (\texttt{wait()} and \texttt{notify()}) are deployed explicitly and selectively to suspend execution without hoarding monitors.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class SafeRunnable implements Runnable {
    private volatile boolean active = true;
    private volatile boolean paused = false;

    @Override
    public void run() {
        while (active) {
            // Synchronized block used strictly to safely park the thread
            synchronized (this) {
                while (paused && active) {
                    try {
                        wait(); // Releases the monitor lock while waiting
                    } catch (InterruptedException e) {
                        active = false; 
                    }
                }
            }

            if (!active) break;

            // --- Actual core work of the thread goes here ---
            System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName() + " is running...");
            
            try {
                Thread.sleep(200); // Standard processing simulation interval
            } catch (InterruptedException e) {
                active = false;
            }
        }
        System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName() + " clean termination complete.");
    }

    // Safe substitute for suspend()
    public synchronized void safeSuspend() {
        paused = true;
    }

    // Safe substitute for resume()
    public synchronized void safeResume() {
        if (paused) {
            paused = false;
            notify(); // Target execution guard; only signals when thread is paused
        }
    }

    // Safe substitute for stop()
    public void safeStop() {
        active = false;
        safeResume(); // Unblocks the thread immediately if it was parked in wait()
    }
}

public class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException {
        SafeRunnable runnable = new SafeRunnable();
        Thread worker = new Thread(runnable, "WorkerThread");
        worker.start();

        Thread.sleep(600);
        System.out.println("[Main] Suspending thread...");
        runnable.safeSuspend();

        Thread.sleep(1000);
        System.out.println("[Main] Resuming thread...");
        runnable.safeResume();

        Thread.sleep(600);
        System.out.println("[Main] Stopping thread cleanly...");
        runnable.safeStop();
        
        worker.join();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item ``Oracle recommends that calls to \texttt{wait()} should take place within a loop that checks the conditions'' --- Why? \mk{5}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2015--16}

%% ── Answer: wait() inside a loop ────────────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Why \texttt{wait()} Must Be Inside a Loop}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

Oracle recommends placing \texttt{wait()} inside a \texttt{while}
loop that re-checks the condition for two reasons:

\medskip
\textbf{1. Spurious wake-ups}

The Java specification explicitly permits a thread to wake up from
\texttt{wait()} \emph{without any call to \texttt{notify()} or
\texttt{notifyAll()}}.  This is called a \textbf{spurious wake-up}
and can occur due to low-level OS signal interruptions.  If
\texttt{wait()} is inside an \texttt{if}, the thread proceeds
even though the condition it was waiting for may still be false.

\medskip
\textbf{2. \texttt{notifyAll()} wakes too many threads}

When \texttt{notifyAll()} is used, \emph{all} waiting threads wake
up.  Only one of them may actually find the condition satisfied; the
rest must go back to waiting.  An \texttt{if} check causes those
threads to proceed incorrectly, while a \texttt{while} loop sends
them back to \texttt{wait()}.

\medskip
\textbf{Illustration:}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// WRONG -- if-based check
public synchronized void consume() throws InterruptedException {
    if (!hasData) wait();   // spurious wake-up or notifyAll can
                            // bypass this check incorrectly
    process(data);
}

// CORRECT -- while-based check
public synchronized void consume() throws InterruptedException {
    while (!hasData) wait(); // always re-checks after waking up
    process(data);
}
\end{lstlisting}

The \texttt{while} loop turns \texttt{wait()} into a self-correcting
mechanism: no matter why the thread woke up --- real notification,
spurious wake, or \texttt{notifyAll()} --- it re-evaluates the
condition and waits again if the condition is still false.

\end{tcolorbox}

\item You are using a 3rd party package called \texttt{Sophisticated} that defines the following classes:
\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{SophisticatedProblemsSolver}
    \item \texttt{SophisticatedProblem}
    \item \texttt{SimpleResult}
\end{itemize}
\texttt{SophisticatedProblemsSolver} has a public method with the following signature:
\begin{center}
    \texttt{public SimpleResult Solve(SophisticatedProblem problem)}
\centerline{}
\end{center}
Your scenario is multi-threaded but you are unsure if \texttt{Solve()} is thread-safe. The following classes written by you need to use this method:
\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{CompetativeProgrammingProblemsSolver}
    \item \texttt{SoftwareDevelopmentProblemSolver}
    \item \texttt{PassInTheExamsProblemSolver}
\end{itemize}
Each of the above classes needs to interact with the same instance of \texttt{SophisticatedProblemsSolver}. The constructors of these classes are passed in a reference of \texttt{SophisticatedProblemsSolver} type. Demonstrate a solution to guarantee that your program will be thread-safe. Write necessary code and provide explanations where appropriate. (Do not use static variables in your solution. Note: You do not have source code for the package \texttt{Sophisticated}) \mk{15}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2015--16}

%% ── Answer: Thread-Safe Synchronization on Shared Object Instance ───
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Thread-Safe Cooperation on a Shared Object Reference}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\textbf{Synchronization Strategy:}
Since the problem states that the constructors of our classes must directly accept a reference of type \texttt{SophisticatedProblemsSolver}, we cannot wrap it in an external container class. Instead, because all three classes share the exact same object reference in memory, we can use a **synchronized block** anchored directly onto that shared reference (\texttt{synchronized(solver)}). 

This approach acts as a mutual-exclusion lock, ensuring that only one thread can invoke \texttt{Solve()} at any given time, thus eliminating data races without utilizing any prohibited static variables.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// --- Mock placeholders for the unmodifiable 3rd party package ---
class SophisticatedProblem {}
class SimpleResult {}
class SophisticatedProblemsSolver {
    public SimpleResult Solve(SophisticatedProblem problem) {
        // Unknown implementation detail -- assumed unsafe
        return new SimpleResult();
    }
}

// --- Class 1: Competitive Programming Problems Solver ---
class CompetativeProgrammingProblemsSolver implements Runnable {
    private final SophisticatedProblemsSolver solver;

    // Constructor accepts standard reference as specified
    public CompetativeProgrammingProblemsSolver(SophisticatedProblemsSolver solver) {
        this.solver = solver;
    }

    @Override
    public void run() {
        SophisticatedProblem problem = new SophisticatedProblem();
        SimpleResult result;

        // Synchronize on the shared instance to serialize calls to Solve()
        synchronized (solver) {
            result = solver.Solve(problem);
        }
        System.out.println("CP Solver finished processing.");
    }
}

// --- Class 2: Software Development Problem Solver ---
class SoftwareDevelopmentProblemSolver implements Runnable {
    private final SophisticatedProblemsSolver solver;

    public SoftwareDevelopmentProblemSolver(SophisticatedProblemsSolver solver) {
        this.solver = solver;
    }

    @Override
    public void run() {
        SophisticatedProblem problem = new SophisticatedProblem();
        SimpleResult result;

        synchronized (solver) {
            result = solver.Solve(problem);
        }
        System.out.println("SD Solver finished processing.");
    }
}

// --- Class 3: Pass In The Exams Problem Solver ---
class PassInTheExamsProblemSolver implements Runnable {
    private final SophisticatedProblemsSolver solver;

    public PassInTheExamsProblemSolver(SophisticatedProblemsSolver solver) {
        this.solver = solver;
    }

    @Override
    public void run() {
        SophisticatedProblem problem = new SophisticatedProblem();
        SimpleResult result;

        synchronized (solver) {
            result = solver.Solve(problem);
        }
        System.out.println("Exam Solver finished processing.");
    }
}

// --- Demonstration Main Class ---
public class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        // Step 1: Create a single shared instance of the un-thread-safe solver
        SophisticatedProblemsSolver sharedSolver = new SophisticatedProblemsSolver();

        // Step 2: Pass the same instance to all consumer constructors
        Thread t1 = new Thread(new CompetativeProgrammingProblemsSolver(sharedSolver));
        Thread t2 = new Thread(new SoftwareDevelopmentProblemSolver(sharedSolver));
        Thread t3 = new Thread(new PassInTheExamsProblemSolver(sharedSolver));

        // Step 3: Execute tasks concurrently
        t1.start();
        t2.start();
        t3.start();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{Why this guarantees Thread Safety:}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{Object Monitor Locking:} Java objects have an intrinsic lock. By wrapping the invocation within \texttt{synchronized(solver)}, a thread must successfully acquire the monitor lock belonging to that specific \texttt{sharedSolver} instance before executing \texttt{Solve()}.
    \item \textbf{No Static Leakage:} The synchronization context relies entirely on the heap lifecycle instance passed through standard object-oriented instantiation, fully avoiding static state variables.
    \item \textbf{Black-Box Compliant:} It requires zero access to or changes inside the unmodifiable \texttt{Sophisticated} package source code.
\end{itemize}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Draw the life-cycle / schematic diagram of different states of a Thread. \mk{9}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2013--14, 2008--09, 2007--08}

%% ── Answer: Thread Life-Cycle ───────────────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
 colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
 title={\textbf{Answer — Thread Life-Cycle (State Diagram)}},
 fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

A Java thread passes through the following states during its lifetime:
\medskip


\begin{center}
    
\begin{tikzpicture}[
    >=Stealth,
    % Base style for all large nodes
    state/.style={
        ellipse, 
        draw=white, 
        thick, 
        text=white, 
        font=\bfseries, 
        minimum width=2.8cm, 
        minimum height=1.2cm, 
        align=center
    },
    % Specific color styles
    blue state/.style={state, fill=nodeblue, draw=blue!50!black},
    orange state/.style={state, fill=nodeorange, draw=orange!60!black},
    green state/.style={state, fill=nodegreen, draw=green!50!black},
    % Small start and end points
    startend/.style={
        circle, 
        fill=nodeblue, 
        draw=blue!60!black, 
        thick, 
        minimum size=0.5cm, 
        inner sep=0pt
    },
    % Arrow and label styles
    arrow/.style={->, draw=lineblue, thick},
    lbl/.style={font=\scriptsize\bfseries, text=black}
]

% 1. Draw the background Scheduler area first so it sits behind the nodes
\node[ellipse, fill=bgorange, draw=orange!40, thick, minimum width=6.5cm, minimum height=4.5cm] (scheduler) at (1.5, 0.5) {};
\node[font=\bfseries, text=black] at (1.5, 0.5) {Scheduler};

% 2. Position all the Nodes
\node[startend] (start) at (-6, 5) {};
\node[blue state] (new) at (-4, 3.5) {New};

\node[orange state] (ready) at (0, 1.5) {Ready-to-Run};
\node[green state] (running) at (3, -0.5) {Running};

\node[blue state] (sleeping) at (5, 3.5) {Sleeping};
\node[blue state] (waiting) at (-4, 0) {Waiting};
\node[blue state] (blocking) at (-1.5, -3) {Blocking};
\node[blue state] (dead) at (6, -3) {Dead};
\node[startend] (end) at (8, -5) {};

% 3. Draw the Paths (Arrows) with Labels
% Start -> New
\draw[arrow] (start) to[out=-60, in=120] node[above right, lbl, pos=0.3] {construct} (new);

% New -> Ready
\draw[arrow] (new) to[out=0, in=135] node[above, lbl] {Thread.start()} (ready);

% Ready <-> Running Loop
\draw[arrow] (ready) to[out=-10, in=140] (running);
\draw[arrow] (running) to[out=170, in=-50] (ready);

% Running <-> Sleeping
\draw[arrow] (running) to[out=40, in=-70] node[right, lbl] {Thread.sleep()} (sleeping);
\draw[arrow] (sleeping) to[out=180, in=40] node[above left, lbl, align=left, pos=0.4] {interrupt() or\\Elapsed Time ends} (ready);

% Running <-> Waiting
\draw[arrow] (running) to[out=-150, in=-60, looseness=1.2] node[above, lbl, pos=0.4] {lock.wait()} (waiting);
\draw[arrow] (waiting) to[out=60, in=180] node[left, lbl, align=right, pos=0.5, yshift=0.2cm] {lock.notify()\\lock.notifyAll()} (ready);

% Running <-> Blocking
\draw[arrow] (running) to[out=-90, in=10] node[right, lbl, align=left, pos=0.4] {Block on I/O\\or locked Monitor\\(Synchronize block)} (blocking);
\draw[arrow] (blocking) to[out=170, in=220, looseness=1.2] node[left, lbl, align=right, pos=0.6, yshift=-0.2cm] {lock acquired\\or I/O completed} (ready);

% Running -> Dead -> End
\draw[arrow] (running) to[out=-30, in=135] node[right, lbl, align=left, pos=0.4, yshift=0.1cm] {run() completes\\or exit()} (dead);
\draw[arrow] (dead) to[out=-60, in=135] (end);

\end{tikzpicture}
\end{center}



\medskip

\textbf{Description of each state:}

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textbf{\arabic*.}]
 \item \textbf{New} --- The thread object has been created (constructed), but \texttt{Thread.start()} has not yet been called.

 \item \textbf{Ready-to-Run} --- \texttt{Thread.start()} has been called. The thread is ready to execute and is waiting in a pool for the \textbf{Scheduler} to assign it CPU time.

 \item \textbf{Running} --- The \textbf{Scheduler} has selected the thread from the Ready-to-Run state and it is currently executing its \texttt{run()} method.

 \item \textbf{Sleeping} --- The thread transitions here when \texttt{Thread.sleep()} is called. It returns to the Ready-to-Run state once the specified elapsed time ends or if \texttt{interrupt()} is called.

 \item \textbf{Waiting} --- The thread goes into this state by calling \texttt{lock.wait()}. It remains here until another thread wakes it up by calling \texttt{lock.notify()} or \texttt{lock.notifyAll()}, after which it goes back to Ready-to-Run.

 \item \textbf{Blocking} --- A thread is blocked when it is waiting for an I/O operation to complete or waiting to acquire a locked Monitor (e.g., entering a \texttt{synchronized} block). It returns to Ready-to-Run when the I/O is completed or the lock is acquired.

 \item \textbf{Dead} --- The thread enters this final state when its \texttt{run()} method completes or it forcibly exits. A dead thread cannot be restarted.
\end{enumerate}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Discuss ``runnable'' and ``waiting'' states of Thread briefly. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2013--14}

%% ── Answer: Runnable and Waiting states ─────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer — Runnable and Waiting States}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\textbf{Runnable State}

A thread enters the \emph{Runnable} state as soon as \texttt{start()}
is invoked on it.  In this state the thread is \emph{eligible to run}
but is not necessarily executing at this instant; it is queued and
awaiting CPU time from the JVM thread scheduler.

\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item A thread also returns to \emph{Runnable} after waking up from
    a \texttt{sleep()}, after being notified out of a \texttt{wait()},
    or after a blocking I/O operation completes.
  \item Multiple threads can be in the \emph{Runnable} state
    simultaneously; the scheduler picks one to move to
    \emph{Running}.
  \item A \emph{Running} thread may be pre-empted (moved back to
    \emph{Runnable}) at any time by the scheduler to give another
    thread a turn.
\end{itemize}

\medskip
\textbf{Waiting State}

A thread enters the \emph{Waiting} state when it voluntarily suspends
itself and cannot proceed until some external condition is satisfied:

\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item \texttt{Object.wait()} --- thread releases the monitor lock
    and waits until another thread calls \texttt{notify()} or
    \texttt{notifyAll()} on the same object.
  \item \texttt{Thread.join()} --- the calling thread waits
    indefinitely for the target thread to terminate.
  \item \texttt{LockSupport.park()} --- low-level parking used
    internally by \texttt{java.util.concurrent} utilities.
\end{itemize}

A \emph{Waiting} thread holds \textbf{no} lock and consumes no CPU.
It transitions back to \emph{Runnable} only when:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),itemsep=1pt]
  \item another thread calls \texttt{notify()} / \texttt{notifyAll()},
  \item the joined thread terminates, or
  \item the waiting thread is interrupted.
\end{enumerate}

\medskip
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Aspect} & \textbf{Runnable} & \textbf{Waiting} \\
\midrule
CPU usage     & May use CPU    & No CPU usage \\
Lock held     & Possible       & No lock held \\
How to exit   & Scheduler picks it & \texttt{notify()} / join completes \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Why may deadlocks occur while developing a user interface? Write a program to show how this can be mitigated. \mk{4+7}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2013--14}

%% ── Answer: UI deadlock ─────────────────────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Deadlocks in UI and How to Mitigate Them}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\textbf{Why deadlocks occur in UI programs:}

Java Swing (and AWT) is \textbf{single-threaded}: all UI operations
must run on the \emph{Event Dispatch Thread} (EDT).  A deadlock
occurs when:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*),itemsep=2pt]
  \item A background thread holds a lock \textbf{A} and tries to
    update the UI, so it calls \texttt{SwingUtilities.invokeAndWait()}
    to schedule work on the EDT and then \emph{blocks waiting} for
    the EDT to finish.
  \item The EDT is simultaneously trying to acquire lock \textbf{A}
    (e.g.\ to read shared data before a repaint).
  \item Both threads wait for each other --- \textbf{deadlock}.
\end{enumerate}

\medskip
\textbf{Mitigation --- use \texttt{invokeLater} instead of
\texttt{invokeAndWait}, and keep locks short:}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import javax.swing.*;
import java.awt.*;

class SharedModel {
    private String value = "initial";

    public synchronized void setValue(String v) { value = v; }
    public synchronized String getValue()       { return value; }
}

public class UIDeadlockDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        SharedModel model = new SharedModel();
        JLabel label = new JLabel(model.getValue());
        JFrame frame = new JFrame("Safe UI Update");
        frame.setDefaultCloseOperation(JFrame.EXIT_ON_CLOSE);
        frame.add(label, BorderLayout.CENTER);
        frame.setSize(300, 100);
        frame.setVisible(true);

        // Background thread updates the model, then schedules
        // UI refresh on EDT using invokeLater (non-blocking).
        // It does NOT hold any lock while calling invokeLater,
        // so the EDT can freely acquire the model's lock.
        Thread worker = new Thread(() -> {
            for (int i = 1; i <= 10; i++) {
                model.setValue("Step " + i);    // short lock

                // invokeLater: background thread does NOT block
                String snapshot = model.getValue(); // read outside EDT
                SwingUtilities.invokeLater(
                    () -> label.setText(snapshot)  // EDT updates UI
                );

                try { Thread.sleep(500); }
                catch (InterruptedException e) {}
            }
        });
        worker.setDaemon(true);
        worker.start();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Key rules to prevent UI deadlocks:}
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item Never call \texttt{invokeAndWait()} while holding a lock that
    the EDT might need.
  \item Prefer \texttt{invokeLater()} (fire-and-forget) over
    \texttt{invokeAndWait()} (blocking).
  \item Keep lock scopes as small as possible --- read shared data,
    release the lock, then schedule the UI update.
\end{itemize}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Write a Java code to solve the Producer-Consumer problem where two threads share a common buffer of size 1. Use inter-thread communication with synchronized monitor. \mk{18}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2011--12}
\variant{CSE 201 | 2007--08}

%% ── Answer: Producer-Consumer buffer size 1 ─────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Producer-Consumer: Buffer Size 1, Synchronized Monitor}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class SharedBuffer {
    private int data;
    private boolean hasData = false;

    // Producer calls this
    public synchronized void produce(int value)
            throws InterruptedException {
        while (hasData) wait();     // wait until Consumer reads
        data    = value;
        hasData = true;
        System.out.println("Produced: " + value);
        notifyAll();                // wake Consumer
    }

    // Consumer calls this
    public synchronized int consume()
            throws InterruptedException {
        while (!hasData) wait();    // wait until Producer writes
        hasData = false;
        System.out.println("Consumed: " + data);
        notifyAll();                // wake Producer
        return data;
    }
}

class Producer extends Thread {
    private final SharedBuffer buf;
    Producer(SharedBuffer buf) { this.buf = buf; }
    @Override
    public void run() {
        try {
            for (int i = 1; i <= 10; i++) buf.produce(i);
        } catch (InterruptedException e) {}
    }
}

class Consumer extends Thread {
    private final SharedBuffer buf;
    Consumer(SharedBuffer buf) { this.buf = buf; }
    @Override
    public void run() {
        try {
            for (int i = 0; i < 10; i++) buf.consume();
        } catch (InterruptedException e) {}
    }
}

public class ProducerConsumerDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        SharedBuffer buf = new SharedBuffer();
        new Producer(buf).start();
        new Consumer(buf).start();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{How it works:}
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item The buffer holds exactly one integer at a time
    (\texttt{hasData} flag acts as the full/empty indicator).
  \item \texttt{produce()} blocks with \texttt{wait()} if
    \texttt{hasData} is \texttt{true}; \texttt{consume()} blocks if
    \texttt{hasData} is \texttt{false}.
  \item After each read/write, \texttt{notifyAll()} unblocks the
    waiting partner thread.
\end{itemize}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Give an example of a multithreaded Java program using the \texttt{Runnable} interface. You must ensure that the main thread terminates last. Mention two different ways to achieve synchronization among threads in Java. \mk{6+4}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2010--11}

%% ── Answer: Runnable example + main terminates last ─────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer — Multithreaded Program with \texttt{Runnable}; Main Terminates Last}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class PrintTask implements Runnable {
    private final String name;
    PrintTask(String name) { this.name = name; }

    @Override
    public void run() {
        for (int i = 1; i <= 4; i++) {
            System.out.println(name + " -> step " + i);
            try { Thread.sleep(100); } catch (InterruptedException e) {}
        }
        System.out.println(name + " finished.");
    }
}

public class RunnableDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Thread t1 = new Thread(new PrintTask("Worker-1"));
        Thread t2 = new Thread(new PrintTask("Worker-2"));
        Thread t3 = new Thread(new PrintTask("Worker-3"));

        t1.start();
        t2.start();
        t3.start();

        // join() ensures main waits until each worker finishes
        try {
            t1.join();
            t2.join();
            t3.join();
        } catch (InterruptedException e) {
            e.printStackTrace();
        }

        System.out.println("Main thread terminates last.");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{How main terminates last:}  \texttt{Thread.join()} causes the
calling thread (here, \texttt{main}) to suspend until the specified
thread completes.  By calling \texttt{join()} on every worker before
printing the final message, we guarantee that all workers have
finished before \texttt{main} exits.

\medskip
\textcolor{cB}{\rule{\textwidth}{0.4pt}}
\medskip

\textbf{Two ways to achieve synchronisation:}

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textbf{\arabic*.}]
  \item \textbf{Synchronized method} --- declare a method with the
    \texttt{synchronized} keyword; the entire method body becomes a
    critical section locked on \texttt{this}.

  \item \textbf{Synchronized statement (block)} --- wrap only the
    shared-resource access inside \texttt{synchronized(obj)\{\}};
    allows a more targeted lock with a programmer-chosen object.
\end{enumerate}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item When is it a must to implement multithreading with the \texttt{Runnable} interface instead of extending the \texttt{Thread} class? Give a simple example of a multithreaded Java program using the \texttt{Runnable} interface. \mk{15}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2009--10}

%% ── Answer: Must use Runnable + example ─────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer — When \texttt{Runnable} is Mandatory}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\textbf{When is \texttt{Runnable} mandatory?}

It is \emph{compulsory} to implement \texttt{Runnable} (rather than
extending \texttt{Thread}) when the class that is to be run as a thread
\textbf{already extends another class}.

Because Java supports only \emph{single inheritance}, a class cannot
extend both \texttt{Thread} and another base class simultaneously.
Implementing \texttt{Runnable} is the only option in this case.

\medskip
\textbf{Example — a class that must extend another class:}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// Suppose we have an existing base class
class Animal {
    String sound;
    Animal(String sound) { this.sound = sound; }
    public void makeSound() { System.out.println(sound); }
}

// Dog must extend Animal AND run as a thread.
// Extending Thread is NOT possible here because Java has
// single inheritance.  Implementing Runnable is the only way.
class Dog extends Animal implements Runnable {
    private int times;

    Dog(String sound, int times) {
        super(sound);
        this.times = times;
    }

    @Override
    public void run() {
        for (int i = 0; i < times; i++) {
            makeSound();
            try { Thread.sleep(200); } catch (InterruptedException e) {}
        }
    }
}

public class RunnableMustDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws InterruptedException {
        Dog dog1 = new Dog("Woof!", 3);
        Dog dog2 = new Dog("Bark!", 3);

        Thread t1 = new Thread(dog1);
        Thread t2 = new Thread(dog2);

        t1.start();
        t2.start();

        t1.join();
        t2.join();

        System.out.println("All dogs done. Main exits last.");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Other reasons to prefer \texttt{Runnable} even when not strictly
required:}
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item Separates the task (what to do) from the thread (how to run it).
  \item The same \texttt{Runnable} instance can be submitted to thread
    pools (\texttt{ExecutorService}) without modification.
  \item Promotes better OOP design — extend a class only when you are
    specialising its behaviour.
\end{itemize}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Define a circular \texttt{Queue} class that can be safely shared by multiple threads. Define \texttt{Producer} and \texttt{Consumer} classes extending Thread. Write a \texttt{Test} class with one Queue but several producers and consumers. \mk{20}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2009--10}

%% ── Answer: Thread-safe circular Queue with producers & consumers ────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Thread-Safe Circular Queue with Multiple Producers \& Consumers}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class Queue {
    private final int[] buffer;
    private int head = 0, tail = 0, count = 0;
    private final int capacity;

    Queue(int capacity) {
        this.capacity = capacity;
        this.buffer   = new int[capacity];
    }

    public synchronized void enqueue(int item)
            throws InterruptedException {
        while (count == capacity) wait(); // full -- producer waits
        buffer[tail] = item;
        tail  = (tail + 1) % capacity;   // wrap around
        count++;
        System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName()
                           + " enqueued " + item);
        notifyAll();
    }

    public synchronized int dequeue() throws InterruptedException {
        while (count == 0) wait();        // empty -- consumer waits
        int item = buffer[head];
        head  = (head + 1) % capacity;   // wrap around
        count--;
        System.out.println(Thread.currentThread().getName()
                           + " dequeued " + item);
        notifyAll();
        return item;
    }
}

class Producer extends Thread {
    private final Queue queue;
    private final int id;
    Producer(Queue queue, int id) {
        super("Producer-" + id);
        this.queue = queue; this.id = id;
    }
    @Override
    public void run() {
        try {
            for (int i = 0; i < 5; i++) {
                queue.enqueue(id * 100 + i);
                Thread.sleep(100);
            }
        } catch (InterruptedException e) {}
    }
}

class Consumer extends Thread {
    private final Queue queue;
    Consumer(Queue queue, int id) {
        super("Consumer-" + id);
        this.queue = queue;
    }
    @Override
    public void run() {
        try {
            for (int i = 0; i < 5; i++) {
                queue.dequeue();
                Thread.sleep(150);
            }
        } catch (InterruptedException e) {}
    }
}

class Test {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Queue q = new Queue(5); // circular buffer of size 5

        // Multiple producers and consumers
        Producer p1 = new Producer(q, 1);
        Producer p2 = new Producer(q, 2);
        Consumer c1 = new Consumer(q, 1);
        Consumer c2 = new Consumer(q, 2);

        p1.start(); p2.start();
        c1.start(); c2.start();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Design notes:}
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item The circular buffer uses \texttt{head}, \texttt{tail}, and
    \texttt{count} to track the queue state; modular arithmetic
    (\texttt{\%\,capacity}) wraps the pointers.
  \item All shared state is accessed inside \texttt{synchronized}
    methods, ensuring mutual exclusion.
  \item \texttt{notifyAll()} wakes all waiting threads; each then
    re-checks its \texttt{while} condition before proceeding.
\end{itemize}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item What do you know about Thread Synchronization? What are the two ways to achieve synchronization? \mk{8}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2008--09}

%% ── Answer: Thread Synchronisation (detailed) ───────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cF!4,colframe=cF,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer — Thread Synchronisation}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cF]

\textbf{What is Thread Synchronisation?}

When two or more threads share access to a common resource (e.g.\ a
shared variable, file, or data structure), concurrent modifications
can leave the resource in an inconsistent state — a situation called
a \emph{race condition}.  \textbf{Thread synchronisation} is the
mechanism by which only \emph{one thread at a time} is permitted to
access a critical section of code, thereby preventing race conditions
and ensuring data integrity.

Java implements synchronisation using \emph{monitors}: every Java
object has an implicit monitor (intrinsic lock).  A thread that enters
a \texttt{synchronized} region must first acquire the object's monitor;
all other threads trying to enter the same region block until the
lock is released.

\medskip
\textbf{Two ways to achieve synchronisation in Java:}

\medskip
\textbf{Way 1 --- Synchronized method}

Place the \texttt{synchronized} keyword in the method signature.  The
lock is the \texttt{this} reference (or the \texttt{Class} object for
\texttt{static} methods).

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class SharedBank {
    private double balance;

    public synchronized void deposit(double amount) {
        balance += amount;
    }
    public synchronized double getBalance() {
        return balance;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{Way 2 --- Synchronized statement (block)}

Enclose only the critical section with \texttt{synchronized(lockObj)}.
The programmer explicitly specifies the lock object.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class SharedBank {
    private double balance;
    private final Object lock = new Object();

    public void deposit(double amount) {
        // logging, validation, etc. run here -- no lock held
        synchronized (lock) {
            balance += amount;
        }
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{Comparison:}

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}p{0.44\linewidth}p{0.44\linewidth}@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Synchronized method} & \textbf{Synchronized block} \\
\midrule
Entire method is locked & Only the critical section is locked \\
Lock object is always \texttt{this} & Any object can be the lock \\
Simpler to write & More flexible and fine-grained \\
Higher contention & Lower contention \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\end{tcolorbox}


\end{enumerate}
\newpage

%%══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
