\markboth{S15 --- Generics \& Collections}{}
\label{sec:S15}
\titleformat{\section}{\large\bfseries\color{cG}}{}{0em}{}[\titlerule]
\section{S15 --- Generics \& Collections}

\begin{enumerate}
\item Implement the \texttt{MyMax} class to achieve the provided output for the main method with the following restrictions:
\begin{enumerate}
    \item \texttt{MyMax} class can only be created for Java number classes.
    \item The implementation of methods \texttt{sameMax1} and \texttt{sameMax2} will be different.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public class MyMaxTest {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Long[] n1 = {10L, 20L, 30L, 40L, 50L};
        MyMax<Long> mx1 = new MyMax<>(n1);
        System.out.println(mx1.max()); // 50.0

        Float[] n2 = {50.0f, 20.0f, 40.0f, 10.0f, 30.0f};
        MyMax<Float> mx2 = new MyMax<>(n2);
        System.out.println(mx2.max()); // 50.0

        Double[] n3 = {50.0, 20.0, 40.0, 10.0, 30.0};
        MyMax<Double> mx3 = new MyMax<>(n3);
        System.out.println(mx3.max()); // 50.0

        System.out.println(mx1.sameMax1(mx2)); // true
        System.out.println(mx2.sameMax2(mx3)); // true
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2023--24}

%% -- Q15 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- MyMax with sameMax1 and sameMax2}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class MyMax<T extends Number & Comparable<T>> {
    private T[] data;

    MyMax(T[] data) { this.data = data; }

    double max() {
        T m = data[0];
        for (T t : data)
            if (t.compareTo(m) > 0) m = t;
        return m.doubleValue();
    }

    // sameMax1: compares via Double.compare (exact equality check)
    boolean sameMax1(MyMax<? extends Number> other) {
        return Double.compare(this.max(), other.max()) == 0;
    }

    // sameMax2: compares via subtraction with epsilon tolerance
    boolean sameMax2(Object o) {
        if(!(o instanceof MyMax)) return false;
        MyMax<? extends Number> other = (MyMax<? extends Number>) o;
        
        return Math.abs(this.max() - other.max()) < 1e-9;
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\item Write two/three differences between \texttt{ArrayList} and \texttt{Vector}. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2016--17, 2021--22, 2022--23}
\variant{CSE 107 | Jan 2021, 2020--21}

%% -- Q1 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- ArrayList vs Vector}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Feature} & \textbf{ArrayList} & \textbf{Vector} \\
\midrule
Synchronization & Not synchronized (not thread-safe) & Synchronized (thread-safe) \\
Performance     & Faster (no sync overhead)           & Slower due to locking \\
Growth          & Grows by 50\% when full             & Doubles in size when full \\
Legacy          & Introduced in Java 1.2 (modern)     & Legacy class (Java 1.0) \\
Iterator        & Uses \texttt{Iterator} / \texttt{ListIterator} & Also supports \texttt{Enumeration} \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip
\textbf{Recommendation:} Prefer \texttt{ArrayList} for single-threaded
use. For thread safety, use \texttt{Collections.synchronizedList()} or
\texttt{CopyOnWriteArrayList} instead of \texttt{Vector}.
\end{tcolorbox}



\item Write three differences between \texttt{Hashtable} and \texttt{HashMap}. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2016--17, 2017--18, 2019--20, 2022--23}

%% -- Q2 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Hashtable vs HashMap}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabularx}{\linewidth}{@{}llX@{}}
\toprule
\textbf{Feature}    & \textbf{Hashtable}              & \textbf{HashMap} \\
\midrule
Null keys/values    & Neither key nor value can be null & One null key, multiple null values allowed \\
Synchronization     & Synchronized (thread-safe)        & Not synchronized \\
Performance         & Slower due to locking             & Faster \\
Legacy              & Legacy class (Java 1.0)           & Modern (Java 1.2) \\
Iteration order     & No guaranteed order               & No guaranteed order \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabularx}
\end{center}

\medskip
\textbf{Example showing null:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
HashMap<String, Double> map = new HashMap<>();
map.put(null, 100.0);        // OK
map.put("Alice", null);      // OK

Hashtable<String, Double> ht = new Hashtable<>();
// ht.put(null, 100.0);     // NullPointerException!
// ht.put("Alice", null);   // NullPointerException!
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}



\item Create an appropriate Hash-based collection to store IPL players (Pat Cummins: 17{,}300{,}000, Kane Williamson: 16{,}000{,}000, MS Dhoni: null). Iterate and print values. Increase Pat Cummins's salary by 500{,}000. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2022--23}
\variant{CSE 107 | 2016--17, 2017--18}


%% -- Q4 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- IPL Players HashMap (Supports null Values)}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]

Since one salary is \texttt{null}, \texttt{HashMap} is required
(\texttt{Hashtable} does not allow null values).

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.HashMap;
import java.util.Map;

class IPLDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        HashMap<String, Integer> players = new HashMap<>();
        players.put("Pat Cummins",     17_300_000);
        players.put("Kane Williamson", 16_000_000);
        players.put("MS Dhoni",        null);       // null salary

        // Iterate and print
        System.out.println("--- IPL Salaries ---");
        for (Map.Entry<String, Integer> e : players.entrySet())
            System.out.println(e.getKey() + ": " + e.getValue());

        // Increase Pat Cummins's salary by 500,000
        players.put("Pat Cummins",
                    players.get("Pat Cummins") + 500_000);

        System.out.println("\nAfter raise:");
        System.out.println("Pat Cummins: " + players.get("Pat Cummins"));
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
--- IPL Salaries ---
Pat Cummins: 17300000
Kane Williamson: 16000000
MS Dhoni: null

After raise:
Pat Cummins: 17800000
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}


\item Write a generic interface \texttt{iQueue} with \texttt{enqueue}, \texttt{dequeue}, \texttt{isEmpty}. Write a generic class \texttt{Queue} implementing \texttt{iQueue}. The interface only supports numeric types. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2019--20, 2022--23}

%% -- Q9 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Generic iQueue Interface and Queue Class (Numeric Only)}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.LinkedList;

// Bounded to Number subclasses (numeric types only)
interface iQueue<T extends Number> {
    void    enqueue(T item);
    T       dequeue();
    boolean isEmpty();
}

class Queue<T extends Number> implements iQueue<T> {
    private LinkedList<T> list = new LinkedList<>();

    @Override
    public void enqueue(T item) { list.addLast(item); }

    @Override
    public T dequeue() {
        if (isEmpty())
            throw new RuntimeException("Queue is empty");
        return list.removeFirst();
    }

    @Override
    public boolean isEmpty() { return list.isEmpty(); }

    @Override
    public String toString() { return list.toString(); }
}

class QueueDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Queue<Integer> q = new Queue<>();
        q.enqueue(10); q.enqueue(20); q.enqueue(30);
        System.out.println("Queue: " + q);
        System.out.println("Dequeue: " + q.dequeue());
        System.out.println("Queue: " + q);

        Queue<Double> dq = new Queue<>();
        dq.enqueue(1.5); dq.enqueue(2.5);
        System.out.println("Double Queue: " + dq);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
Queue: [10, 20, 30]
Dequeue: 10
Queue: [20, 30]
Double Queue: [1.5, 2.5]
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}




\item Implement the \texttt{MyStats} class taking \texttt{List} as input. Can only be created for Java number classes. \texttt{sameAvg1} and \texttt{sameAvg2} must have different implementations:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
Integer[] n1 = {1, 2, 3, 4, 5};
List<Integer> list1 = Arrays.asList(n1);
MyStats<Integer> s1 = new MyStats<>(list1);
System.out.println(s1.average()); // 3.0
Long[] n2 = {5L, 2L, 4L, 1L, 3L};
List<Long> list2 = Arrays.asList(n2);
MyStats<Long> s2 = new MyStats<>(list2);
System.out.println(s2.average()); // 3.0
Double[] n3 = {5.0, 4.0, 3.0, 2.0, 1.0};
List<Double> list3 = Arrays.asList(n3);
MyStats<Double> s3 = new MyStats<>(list3);
System.out.println(s1.sameAvg1(s2)); // true
System.out.println(s2.sameAvg2(s3)); // true
\end{lstlisting}
\mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | Jan 2021, 2022--23}

%% -- Q13 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- MyStats Taking List as Input}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.*;

class MyStats<T extends Number> {
    private List<T> data;

    MyStats(List<T> data) {
        this.data = data;
    }

    double average() {
        double sum = 0.0;
        for (T t : data) {
            sum += t.doubleValue();
        }
        return sum / data.size();
    }

    // sameAvg1: Implementation using a Wildcard (?)
    boolean sameAvg1(MyStats<?> other) {
        return Math.abs(this.average() - other.average()) < 1e-9;
    }

    // sameAvg2: Implementation using a Generic Method Parameter (V)
    <V extends Number> boolean sameAvg2(MyStats<V> other) {
        return Math.abs(this.average() - other.average()) < 1e-9;
    }
}

class MyStatsList {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        List<Integer> list1 = Arrays.asList(1, 2, 3, 4, 5);
        MyStats<Integer> s1 = new MyStats<>(list1);
        System.out.println(s1.average()); // 3.0
        
        List<Long> list2 = Arrays.asList(5L, 2L, 4L, 1L, 3L);
        MyStats<Long> s2 = new MyStats<>(list2);
        System.out.println(s2.average()); // 3.0

        List<Double> list3 = Arrays.asList(5.0, 4.0, 3.0, 2.0, 1.0);
        MyStats<Double> s3 = new MyStats<>(list3);
        
        System.out.println(s1.sameAvg1(s2)); // true
        System.out.println(s2.sameAvg2(s3)); // true
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\item Write two differences between \texttt{ArrayList} and \texttt{Vector}. Consider \texttt{Employee} (attributes: id, name, age). Write necessary Java code so that \texttt{Collections.sort(listEmployees)} sorts by ascending id; if equal, by lexicographic name; if both equal, by ascending age. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2022--23}

%% -- Q18 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Employee Sort: id, name, age}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]

\textbf{Two ArrayList vs Vector differences:} ArrayList is not
synchronized (faster); Vector is. ArrayList grows 50\%; Vector doubles.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.*;

class Employee implements Comparable<Employee> {
    int id; String name; int age;
    Employee(int id, String name, int age) {
        this.id=id; this.name=name; this.age=age;
    }

    @Override
    public int compareTo(Employee o) {
        int c = Integer.compare(this.id, o.id);       // asc id
        if (c != 0) return c;
        c = this.name.compareTo(o.name);              // lex name
        if (c != 0) return c;
        return Integer.compare(this.age, o.age);      // asc age
    }

    @Override
    public String toString() {
        return id + "-" + name + "(" + age + ")";
    }
}

class EmployeeSort {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        ArrayList<Employee> list = new ArrayList<>();
        list.add(new Employee(2, "Zara",  25));
        list.add(new Employee(1, "Bob",   22));
        list.add(new Employee(1, "Alice", 30));
        list.add(new Employee(1, "Alice", 25));

        Collections.sort(list);
        list.forEach(System.out::println);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
1-Alice(25)
1-Alice(30)
1-Bob(22)
2-Zara(25)
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}

\item Implement the \texttt{MyAvg} class. Can only be created for Java number classes. It must support \texttt{average()}, \texttt{sameAvg()} (comparing two same-type objects), and \texttt{sameAvgAny()} (comparing two different-type objects):
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
Integer[] n1 = {10, 20, 30, 40, 50};
MyAvg<Integer> s1 = new MyAvg<>(n1);
System.out.println(s1.average()); // 30.0
Integer[] n2 = {50, 20, 40, 10, 30};
MyAvg<Integer> s2 = new MyAvg<>(n2);
System.out.println(s2.average()); // 30.0
System.out.println(s1.sameAvg(s2)); // true
Double[] n3 = {50.0, 40.0, 30.0, 20.0, 10.0};
MyAvg<Double> s3 = new MyAvg<>(n3);
System.out.println(s3.average()); // 30.0
System.out.println(s2.sameAvgAny(s3)); // true
\end{lstlisting}
\mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2021--22}

%% -- Q14 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- MyAvg with sameAvg and sameAvgAny}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class MyAvg<T extends Number> {
    private T[] data;

    MyAvg(T[] data) { this.data = data; }

    double average() {
        double sum = 0;
        for (T t : data) sum += t.doubleValue();
        return sum / data.length;
    }

    // sameAvg: same type T
    boolean sameAvg(MyAvg<T> other) {
        return Double.compare(this.average(), other.average()) == 0;
    }

    // sameAvgAny: any numeric type (wildcard)
    boolean sameAvgAny(MyAvg<? extends Number> other) {
        return Math.abs(this.average() - other.average()) < 1e-9;
    }
}

class MyAvgDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Integer[] n1 = {10, 20, 30, 40, 50};
        MyAvg<Integer> s1 = new MyAvg<>(n1);
        System.out.println(s1.average());       // 30.0

        Integer[] n2 = {50, 20, 40, 10, 30};
        MyAvg<Integer> s2 = new MyAvg<>(n2);
        System.out.println(s2.average());       // 30.0
        System.out.println(s1.sameAvg(s2));     // true

        Double[] n3 = {50.0, 40.0, 30.0, 20.0, 10.0};
        MyAvg<Double> s3 = new MyAvg<>(n3);
        System.out.println(s3.average());       // 30.0
        System.out.println(s2.sameAvgAny(s3));  // true
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\item Given the following \texttt{Product} class, write Java code to: (i) define \texttt{ArrayList<Product> myProducts}, (ii) generate 4 Products with names \texttt{'A'} to \texttt{'D'} and random prices, (iii) sort \texttt{myProducts} by name in ascending order (you may modify the \texttt{Product} class if necessary):
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class Product {
    private String name; private double price;
    Product(String name, double price) { this.name = name; this.price = price; }
    public String getName() { return this.name; }
    public double getPrice() { return this.price; }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | Jan 2021}

%% -- Q8 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Product Sort by Name Ascending}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.*;

class Product implements Comparable<Product> {
    private String name; private double price;
    Product(String name, double price) { this.name=name; this.price=price; }
    public String getName()  { return name; }
    public double getPrice() { return price; }

    @Override
    public int compareTo(Product o) {
        return this.name.compareTo(o.name); // ascending by name
    }

    @Override
    public String toString() {
        return name + "($" + String.format("%.2f", price) + ")";
    }
}

class ProductSortByName {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Random rand = new Random();

        // (i) Define ArrayList
        ArrayList<Product> myProducts = new ArrayList<>();

        // (ii) Generate 4 products D, B, A, C with random prices
        String[] names = {"D", "B", "A", "C"};
        for (String n : names)
            myProducts.add(new Product(n, 10 + rand.nextDouble() * 90));

        System.out.println("Before: " + myProducts);

        // (iii) Sort by name ascending
        Collections.sort(myProducts);

        System.out.println("After:  " + myProducts);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output (example):}
\begin{verbatim}
Before: [D($45.23), B($78.10), A($12.50), C($67.89)]
After:  [A($12.50), B($78.10), C($67.89), D($45.23)]
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}


\item Write a generic interface \texttt{iStack} with \texttt{push}, \texttt{pop}, \texttt{isEmpty}. Write a generic class \texttt{Stack} implementing \texttt{iStack}. Interface only supports numeric types. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2020--21, 2016--17}
\variant{CSE 107 | 2022--23}

%% -- Q11 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Generic iStack Interface and Stack Class}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.ArrayList;

interface iStack<T extends Number> {
    void    push(T item);
    T       pop();
    boolean isEmpty();
}

class Stack<T extends Number> implements iStack<T> {
    private ArrayList<T> data = new ArrayList<>();

    @Override
    public void push(T item) { data.add(item); }

    @Override
    public T pop() {
        if (isEmpty()) throw new RuntimeException("Stack is empty");
        return data.remove(data.size() - 1);
    }

    @Override
    public boolean isEmpty() { return data.isEmpty(); }

    @Override
    public String toString() { return data.toString(); }
}

class StackDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Stack<Integer> s = new Stack<>();
        s.push(1); s.push(2); s.push(3);
        System.out.println("Stack: " + s);
        System.out.println("Pop: "   + s.pop());
        System.out.println("Pop: "   + s.pop());
        System.out.println("Stack: " + s);
        System.out.println("Empty: " + s.isEmpty());
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
Stack: [1, 2, 3]
Pop: 3
Pop: 2
Stack: [1]
Empty: false
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}



\item What can you say about the following statement?
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public class ABC<S extends Z & Y & X> { }
\end{lstlisting}
\mk{5}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2020--21, 2016--17}

%% -- Q16 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Bounded Type Parameter with Multiple Bounds}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]

The statement declares a generic class \texttt{ABC} with a type
parameter \texttt{S} that is \textbf{bounded by multiple types}:
\texttt{S extends Z \& Y \& X}.

\textbf{Rules for multiple bounds:}
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item \texttt{S} must be a subtype of \textbf{all} listed types.
  \item \textbf{At most one} bound can be a class; the rest must be
  interfaces. The class bound must come \textbf{first}.
  \item If \texttt{Z} is a class, \texttt{Y} and \texttt{X} must be
  interfaces. If all are interfaces, any order is valid.
\end{itemize}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
interface Y { void doY(); }
interface X { void doX(); }
class Z     { void doZ() {} }

// S must extend Z and implement both Y and X
public class ABC<S extends Z & Y & X> {
    void use(S s) {
        s.doZ(); s.doY(); s.doX(); // all accessible
    }
}

class Concrete extends Z implements Y, X {
    public void doY() {}
    public void doX() {}
}

// ABC<Concrete> ok = new ABC<>();  // valid
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\item Write three differences between \texttt{HashMap} and \texttt{Hashtable}. Create an appropriate Hash-based collection to store the following monthly salaries: Sakib Al Hasan: 3{,}00{,}000; Mashrafe Bin Mortaza: null; Mushfiqur Rahim: 2{,}50{,}000. Then increase Sakib Al Hasan's salary by 50{,}000. \mk{3+10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2017--18}

%% -- Q5 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Cricketer Salaries with HashMap}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]

\textbf{Three differences:} HashMap allows null key/value; Hashtable
does not. HashMap is unsynchronized (faster); Hashtable is synchronized.
HashMap is modern (Java 1.2); Hashtable is legacy (Java 1.0).

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.HashMap;
import java.util.Map;

class CricketerSalary {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        // HashMap chosen because Mashrafe's salary is null
        HashMap<String, Integer> salaries = new HashMap<>();
        salaries.put("Sakib Al Hasan",      300_000);
        salaries.put("Mashrafe Bin Mortaza", null);
        salaries.put("Mushfiqur Rahim",      250_000);

        System.out.println("--- Monthly Salaries ---");
        for (Map.Entry<String, Integer> e : salaries.entrySet())
            System.out.println(e.getKey() + ": " + e.getValue());

        // Increase Sakib Al Hasan's salary by 50,000
        salaries.put("Sakib Al Hasan",
                     salaries.get("Sakib Al Hasan") + 50_000);

        System.out.println("\nSakib after raise: "
                           + salaries.get("Sakib Al Hasan"));
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
--- Monthly Salaries ---
Sakib Al Hasan: 300000
Mashrafe Bin Mortaza: null
Mushfiqur Rahim: 250000

Sakib after raise: 350000
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}



\item Write the general syntax for: (i) declaring a generic class in Java, (ii) declaring a reference to a generic class and creating an instance. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2017--18}
%% ── S8-Q6 ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,
  boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Java generic class syntax}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// (i) Declaring a generic class in Java:
class MyGeneric<T> {
    private T data;
    public MyGeneric(T val) { data = val; }
    public T getData()       { return data; }
}

// Bounded type parameter:
class Pair<T extends Comparable<T>> {
    T first, second;
    Pair(T a, T b){ first=a; second=b; }
    T max(){ return first.compareTo(second)>=0 ? first : second; }
}

// (ii) Declaring a reference and creating an instance:
MyGeneric<Integer>  intObj  = new MyGeneric<>(42);
MyGeneric<String>   strObj  = new MyGeneric<>("Hello");
Pair<Double>        pair    = new Pair<>(3.14, 2.71);

System.out.println(intObj.getData()); // 42
System.out.println(strObj.getData()); // Hello
System.out.println(pair.max());       // 3.14
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}


\item Write two differences between \texttt{ArrayList} and \texttt{Vector}. Write three differences between \texttt{Hashtable} and \texttt{HashMap}. Create an appropriate Hash-based collection to store the following weekly salaries: Lionel Messi: 350{,}000; Cristiano Ronaldo: 365{,}000; Neymar: null. Then increase Lionel Messi's balance by 100{,}000. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2016--17}

%% -- Q6 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Footballer Salaries with HashMap}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]

\textbf{ArrayList vs Vector} (2 differences): ArrayList is not
synchronized (faster); Vector is synchronized. ArrayList grows by 50\%;
Vector doubles in size.

\textbf{HashMap vs Hashtable} (3 differences): HashMap allows null
key/value; Hashtable does not. HashMap is unsynchronized; Hashtable is
synchronized. HashMap is modern; Hashtable is legacy.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.HashMap;
import java.util.Map;

class FootballerSalary {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        // HashMap needed because Neymar's salary is null
        HashMap<String, Integer> salaries = new HashMap<>();
        salaries.put("Lionel Messi",      350_000);
        salaries.put("Cristiano Ronaldo", 365_000);
        salaries.put("Neymar",            null);

        System.out.println("--- Weekly Salaries ---");
        for (Map.Entry<String, Integer> e : salaries.entrySet())
            System.out.println(e.getKey() + ": " + e.getValue());

        // Increase Messi's salary by 100,000
        salaries.put("Lionel Messi",
                     salaries.get("Lionel Messi") + 100_000);

        System.out.println("\nMessi after raise: "
                           + salaries.get("Lionel Messi"));
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
--- Weekly Salaries ---
Lionel Messi: 350000
Cristiano Ronaldo: 365000
Neymar: null

Messi after raise: 450000
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}



\item Write a Java program to store student records as a collection of \texttt{Student} objects. The \texttt{Student} class contains \texttt{Name}, \texttt{Age}, and \texttt{CGPA}. Write the class so that the collection can be sorted using Java Collection's \texttt{sort()} method with the following priority: (i) descending CGPA; (ii) if CGPAs are equal, ascending age; (iii) if ages are also equal, lexicographic order of name. \mk{20}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2015--16}

%% -- Q21 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Student Collection Sorted by CGPA, Age, Name}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.*;

class Student implements Comparable<Student> {
    String name; int age; double cgpa;

    Student(String name, int age, double cgpa) {
        this.name=name; this.age=age; this.cgpa=cgpa;
    }

    @Override
    public int compareTo(Student o) {
        int c = Double.compare(o.cgpa, this.cgpa); // desc CGPA
        if (c != 0) return c;
        c = Integer.compare(this.age, o.age);       // asc age
        if (c != 0) return c;
        return this.name.compareTo(o.name);         // lex name
    }

    @Override
    public String toString() {
        return name + "(age=" + age + ",cgpa=" + cgpa + ")";
    }
}

class StudentCollectionSort {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        ArrayList<Student> list = new ArrayList<>();
        list.add(new Student("Alice", 21, 3.8));
        list.add(new Student("Bob",   20, 3.9));
        list.add(new Student("Carol", 22, 3.8));
        list.add(new Student("Dave",  21, 3.8));
        list.add(new Student("Eve",   19, 4.0));

        Collections.sort(list);
        list.forEach(System.out::println);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
Eve(age=19,cgpa=4.0)
Bob(age=20,cgpa=3.9)
Alice(age=21,cgpa=3.8)
Dave(age=21,cgpa=3.8)
Carol(age=22,cgpa=3.8)
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}



\item Write five differences between \texttt{Hashtable} and \texttt{HashMap}. Consider the following bank account information. Write Java code to: (i) create a Hashtable, (ii) store the five entries, (iii) increase John Doe's balance by 100:
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lr} \toprule \textbf{Name} & \textbf{Balance} \\ \midrule John Doe & 3434.34 \\ Tom Smith & 123.22 \\ Jane Baker & 1378.00 \\ Tod Hall & 99.22 \\ Ralph Smith & 19.08 \\ \bottomrule \end{tabular}
\end{center}
\mk{10}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2014--15}

%% -- Q3 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Hashtable with Bank Accounts}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]

\textbf{Five differences} (see Q2 table above; additional points):
null keys/values forbidden in Hashtable; Hashtable is legacy/synchronized;
HashMap is modern/unsynchronized; HashMap allows one null key and multiple
null values; HashMap is generally preferred in new code.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.Hashtable;

class BankDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        // (i) Create Hashtable
        Hashtable<String, Double> accounts = new Hashtable<>();

        // (ii) Store five entries
        accounts.put("John Doe",    3434.34);
        accounts.put("Tom Smith",    123.22);
        accounts.put("Jane Baker",  1378.00);
        accounts.put("Tod Hall",      99.22);
        accounts.put("Ralph Smith",   19.08);

        System.out.println("Before: " + accounts.get("John Doe"));

        // (iii) Increase John Doe's balance by 100
        accounts.put("John Doe", accounts.get("John Doe") + 100);

        System.out.println("After:  " + accounts.get("John Doe"));

        // Print all
        for (String name : accounts.keySet())
            System.out.printf("%-15s %.2f%n",
                              name, accounts.get(name));
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
Before: 3434.34
After:  3534.34
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}



\item Consider the following class. Write Java code to: (i) define \texttt{ArrayList<Product> myProducts}, (ii) generate 5 Products A--E with random prices, (iii) add Product F with price 1000 at index 1, (iv) sort by price ascending:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
class Product {
    private String name; private double price;
    Product(String name, double price) { this.name = name; this.price = price; }
    public String getName() { return this.name; }
    public double getPrice() { return this.price; }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\mk{10}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2014--15}

%% -- Q7 --------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Product ArrayList: Generate, Insert, Sort by Price}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.*;

class Product {
    private String name; private double price;
    Product(String name, double price) { this.name=name; this.price=price; }
    public String getName()  { return name; }
    public double getPrice() { return price; }
    @Override
    public String toString() {
        return name + "($" + String.format("%.2f", price) + ")";
    }
}

class ProductDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        Random rand = new Random();

        // (i) Define ArrayList
        ArrayList<Product> myProducts = new ArrayList<>();

        // (ii) Generate 5 products A-E with random prices
        for (char c = 'A'; c <= 'E'; c++)
            myProducts.add(new Product(String.valueOf(c),
                                       10 + rand.nextDouble() * 90));

        System.out.println("Before insert: " + myProducts);

        // (iii) Add Product F with price 1000 at index 1
        myProducts.add(1, new Product("F", 1000));

        System.out.println("After insert:  " + myProducts);

        // (iv) Sort by price ascending
        myProducts.sort(Comparator.comparingDouble(Product::getPrice));

        System.out.println("After sort:    " + myProducts);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}



\item A class \texttt{Employee} has two member variables: name (\texttt{String}) and age (\texttt{int}). Write the class so an \texttt{ArrayList} of \texttt{Employee} objects can be sorted by either variable. \mk{14}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2013--14}

%% -- Q17 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Employee Sorted by Name or Age}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.*;

class Employee implements Comparable<Employee> {
    String name; int age;
    Employee(String name, int age) { this.name=name; this.age=age; }

    // Natural order: by name
    @Override
    public int compareTo(Employee o) { return this.name.compareTo(o.name); }

    // Comparator for age
    static Comparator<Employee> byAge() {
        return Comparator.comparingInt(e -> e.age);
    }

    @Override
    public String toString() { return name + "(" + age + ")"; }
}

class EmployeeSortDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        ArrayList<Employee> list = new ArrayList<>();
        list.add(new Employee("Zara", 25));
        list.add(new Employee("Alice", 30));
        list.add(new Employee("Bob", 22));

        Collections.sort(list);          // sort by name
        System.out.println("By name: " + list);

        list.sort(Employee.byAge());     // sort by age
        System.out.println("By age:  " + list);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
By name: [Alice(30), Bob(22), Zara(25)]
By age:  [Bob(22), Zara(25), Alice(30)]
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}

\item Write a class \texttt{Student} containing a \texttt{HashMap} with Integer key and List of String as values. Add 3 studentIds as keys with [firstname, lastname] values. Write a method to print all. \mk{13}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2013--14}

%% -- Q19 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Student HashMap with List Values}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.*;

class StudentMap {
    private HashMap<Integer, List<String>> students = new HashMap<>();

    void addStudent(int id, String firstName, String lastName) {
        List<String> names = new ArrayList<>();
        names.add(firstName); names.add(lastName);
        students.put(id, names);
    }

    void printAll() {
        for (Map.Entry<Integer, List<String>> e : students.entrySet())
            System.out.println("ID: " + e.getKey()
                               + " -> " + e.getValue());
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        StudentMap sm = new StudentMap();
        sm.addStudent(1001, "Alice", "Smith");
        sm.addStudent(1002, "Bob",   "Jones");
        sm.addStudent(1003, "Carol", "White");
        sm.printAll();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
ID: 1001 -> [Alice, Smith]
ID: 1002 -> [Bob, Jones]
ID: 1003 -> [Carol, White]
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}

\item Consider a file named `products.txt' containing following information.

\begin{center}
\begin{verbatim}
1,   P1,   T1,   10
2,   P2,   T2,   20
3,   P3,   T1,   30
4,   P4,   T2,   20
5,   P5,   T1,   30
\end{verbatim}
\end{center}

This file represents information of products where the attributes are (id, name, type, price). A single product's information is contained in a single line. You need to do the following.

\begin{itemize}
    \item[(i)] Write a class in Java named Product with necessary attributes.
    \item[(ii)] Write a function in Java to store the products information from this `products.txt' file to an ArrayList of Product named `myProducts'.
    \item[(iii)] Write a function in Java to store the contents of an ArrayList of Product named `myProducts' to a file named `products2.txt' in the same format as given in the `products.txt' file.
\end{itemize}

\mk{4+8+8} \yr{CSE 201 | 2008--09}
%% -- Q20 -------------------------------------------------------------
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cG!4,colframe=cG,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Product Read/Write from File}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cG]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.io.*;
import java.util.*;

// (i) Product class with necessary attributes
class Product {
    int id; 
    String name, type; 
    int price; // using int based on the sample data provided

    Product(int id, String name, String type, int price) {
        this.id = id; 
        this.name = name; 
        this.type = type; 
        this.price = price;
    }

    @Override
    public String toString() {
        return id + ", " + name + ", " + type + ", " + price;
    }
}

class ProductFileDemo {
    // (ii) Function to read products.txt into an ArrayList
    static ArrayList<Product> readProducts(String filename) throws IOException {
        ArrayList<Product> myProducts = new ArrayList<>();
        try (BufferedReader br = new BufferedReader(new FileReader(filename))) {
            String line;
            while ((line = br.readLine()) != null) {
                if(line.trim().isEmpty()) continue;
                String[] p = line.split(",");
                // trimming is necessary because of spaces after commas
                myProducts.add(new Product(
                        Integer.parseInt(p[0].trim()),
                        p[1].trim(), 
                        p[2].trim(), 
                        Integer.parseInt(p[3].trim())
                ));
            }
        }
        return myProducts;
    }

    // (iii) Function to write ArrayList to products2.txt in the same format
    static void writeProducts(ArrayList<Product> myProducts, String filename) 
            throws IOException {
        try (BufferedWriter bw = new BufferedWriter(new FileWriter(filename))) {
            for (Product p : myProducts) {
                bw.write(p.toString());
                bw.newLine();
            }
        }
    }

    public static void main(String[] args) {
        try {
            ArrayList<Product> myProducts = readProducts("products.txt");
            writeProducts(myProducts, "products2.txt");
            System.out.println("Products successfully copied to products2.txt");
        } catch (IOException e) {
            e.printStackTrace();
        }
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\end{enumerate}
\newpage

%% S16 — Stream API, Lambda & Enums
%%══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
\secdivider{Section S16}{Stream API, Lambda \& Enums}{cH}{cH}
\markboth{S16 --- Stream API, Lambda \& Enums}{}
\label{sec:S16}
\titleformat{\section}{\large\bfseries\color{cH}}{}{0em}{}[\titlerule]
\section{S16 --- Stream API, Lambda \& Enums}

\begin{enumerate}
\item Write Java code for the following: (i) Declare an ArrayList of \texttt{Employee}, add 6 employees; (ii) Rewrite two code segments using Java Stream; (iii) Sort by ascending age; if equal, by ascending name:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// Segment 1
List<String> names = new ArrayList<>();
for (Employee e : list) names.add(e.getName());
// Segment 2
List<Employee> employees = new ArrayList<>();
for (Employee e : list) if (e.getAge() <= 20) employees.add(e);
\end{lstlisting}
\mk{15}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2023--24}

%% ── Q3: Employee Stream rewrite ──────────────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cH!4,colframe=cH,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer — Employee Stream Rewrite and
  Sort}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cH]

\textit{(Uses the same \texttt{Employee} class as Q2.)}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.*;
import java.util.stream.*;

public class EmployeeStreamDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {

        // (i) ArrayList<Employee> with 6 employees
        ArrayList<Employee> list = new ArrayList<>();
        list.add(new Employee(1, "Alice",  22));
        list.add(new Employee(2, "Bob",    19));
        list.add(new Employee(3, "Carol",  20));
        list.add(new Employee(4, "Dave",   20));
        list.add(new Employee(5, "Eve",    17));
        list.add(new Employee(6, "Frank",  25));

        // -- Segment 1 (original for-each loop) -----------
        List<String> names1 = new ArrayList<>();
        for (Employee e : list) names1.add(e.getName());

        // (ii-a) Segment 1 using Stream
        List<String> names2 = list.stream()
            .map(Employee::getName)
            .collect(Collectors.toList());

        System.out.println("All names: " + names2);

        // -- Segment 2 (original for-each loop) -----------
        List<Employee> filtered1 = new ArrayList<>();
        for (Employee e : list)
            if (e.getAge() <= 20) filtered1.add(e);

        // (ii-b) Segment 2 using Stream
        List<Employee> filtered2 = list.stream()
            .filter(e -> e.getAge() <= 20)
            .collect(Collectors.toList());

        System.out.println("Age <= 20: " + filtered2);

        // (iii) Sort: ascending age, then ascending name
        list.sort(Comparator.comparingInt(Employee::getAge)
                            .thenComparing(Employee::getName));

        System.out.println("Sorted: " + list);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
All names: [Alice, Bob, Carol, Dave, Eve, Frank]
Age <= 20: [Bob, Carol, Dave, Eve]
Sorted: [5:Eve(17), 2:Bob(19), 3:Carol(20), 4:Dave(20),
         1:Alice(22), 6:Frank(25)]
\end{verbatim}

\end{tcolorbox}


\item Develop Java code for the following using an \texttt{Employee} class (id, name, age): (i) Declare \texttt{ArrayList<Employee>} and add 6 employees; (ii) Store names of employees aged $> 15$ in \texttt{nameList}; (iii) Sort by ascending age; if equal, by ascending name. \mk{15}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2021--22}

%% ── Q2: Employee ArrayList + Stream + Sort ───────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cH!4,colframe=cH,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer — Employee ArrayList, Filter
  and Sort}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cH]

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.*;
import java.util.stream.*;

class Employee {
    private int    id;
    private String name;
    private int    age;

    Employee(int id, String name, int age) {
        this.id = id; this.name = name; this.age = age;
    }
    public int    getId()   { return id;   }
    public String getName() { return name; }
    public int    getAge()  { return age;  }

    @Override
    public String toString() {
        return id + ":" + name + "(" + age + ")";
    }
}

public class EmployeeDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {

        // (i) ArrayList<Employee> with 6 employees
        ArrayList<Employee> list = new ArrayList<>();
        list.add(new Employee(1, "Alice",  22));
        list.add(new Employee(2, "Bob",    14));
        list.add(new Employee(3, "Carol",  19));
        list.add(new Employee(4, "Dave",   30));
        list.add(new Employee(5, "Eve",    16));
        list.add(new Employee(6, "Frank",  25));

        // (ii) Store names of employees aged > 15
        List<String> nameList = list.stream()
            .filter(e -> e.getAge() > 15)
            .map(Employee::getName)
            .collect(Collectors.toList());

        System.out.println("Names (age > 15): " + nameList);

        // (iii) Sort by ascending age; if equal, ascending name
        list.sort(Comparator.comparingInt(Employee::getAge)
                            .thenComparing(Employee::getName));

        System.out.println("Sorted employees: " + list);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
Names (age > 15): [Alice, Carol, Eve, Dave, Frank]
Sorted employees: [2:Bob(14), 5:Eve(16), 3:Carol(19),
                   1:Alice(22), 6:Frank(25), 4:Dave(30)]
\end{verbatim}

\end{tcolorbox}


\item Create a Java enum named \texttt{HttpStatus} to represent the following HTTP status codes: \mk{10}

\begin{verbatim}
OK (200, "OK"), NOT_FOUND (404, "Not Found"),
\end{verbatim}
\begin{verbatim}
 INTERNAL_ERROR (500, "Internal Server Error")
\end{verbatim}

Each enum constant should store two fields: an \texttt{int} status code and a \texttt{String} message.

Your enum should also implement the following methods:
\begin{enumerate}
    \item \texttt{isError()}: Returns false for \texttt{OK}, and true for both \texttt{NOT\_FOUND} and \texttt{INTERNAL\_ERROR}
    \item \texttt{toString()}: Returns a string in the format "200 OK", "404 Not Found", "500 Internal Server Error"
    \item \texttt{fromCode(int code)} (static method): Takes an \texttt{int} code and returns the corresponding \texttt{HttpStatus} constant. If the code doesn't match any defined status, return \texttt{null}.
\end{enumerate}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2023--24}

%% ── Answer: HttpStatus enum ─────────────────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cH!4,colframe=cH,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- \texttt{HttpStatus} Enum}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cH]

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public enum HttpStatus {
    OK(200, "OK"),
    NOT_FOUND(404, "Not Found"),
    INTERNAL_ERROR(500, "Internal Server Error");

    private final int code;
    private final String message;

    // Constructor to store the two fields
    HttpStatus(int code, String message) {
        this.code = code;
        this.message = message;
    }

    // i. isError() method
    public boolean isError() {
        return this != OK;
    }

    // ii. toString() method
    @Override
    public String toString() {
        return code + " " + message;
    }

    // iii. fromCode(int code) static method
    public static HttpStatus fromCode(int code) {
        for (HttpStatus status : HttpStatus.values()) {
            if (status.code == code) {
                return status;
            }
        }
        return null;
    }

    // Demonstration (Optional but helpful for testing)
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        System.out.println(HttpStatus.OK);                   // 200 OK
        System.out.println(HttpStatus.NOT_FOUND);            // 404 Not Found
        System.out.println(HttpStatus.OK.isError());         // false
        System.out.println(HttpStatus.NOT_FOUND.isError());  // true
        System.out.println(HttpStatus.fromCode(500));        // 500 Internal Server Error
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}


\item Consider the following \texttt{Person} class. Write Java code for the following: (i) Declare \texttt{ArrayList<Person> list} and add 6 persons; (ii) Rewrite the two segments using Java Stream; (iii) Sort the list by ascending age, then ascending name if age is equal:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// Segment 1
List<String> names = new ArrayList<>();
for (int i = 0; i < list.size(); i++) { Person mc = list.get(i); names.add(mc.getName()); }
// Segment 2
List<Person> persons = new ArrayList<>();
for (int i = 0; i < list.size(); i++) { Person mc = list.get(i); if (mc.getAge() <= 20) persons.add(mc); }
\end{lstlisting}
\mk{20}
\yr{CSE 107 | Jan 2021}
\variant{CSE 107 | 2021--22, 2022--23, 2023--24}

%% ── Q1: Person Stream + Sort ─────────────────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cH!4,colframe=cH,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer — Person ArrayList, Streams
  and Sorting}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cH]

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.*;
import java.util.stream.*;

class Person {
    private String name;
    private int    age;

    Person(String name, int age) {
        this.name = name; this.age = age;
    }
    public String getName() { return name; }
    public int    getAge()  { return age;  }

    @Override
    public String toString() {
        return name + "(" + age + ")";
    }
}

public class PersonDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {

        // (i) Declare ArrayList<Person> and add 6 persons
        ArrayList<Person> list = new ArrayList<>();
        list.add(new Person("Alice",  22));
        list.add(new Person("Bob",    19));
        list.add(new Person("Carol",  20));
        list.add(new Person("Dave",   20));
        list.add(new Person("Eve",    17));
        list.add(new Person("Frank",  25));

        // -- Original Segment 1 (loop) ---------------------
        List<String> names1 = new ArrayList<>();
        for (int i = 0; i < list.size(); i++) {
            Person mc = list.get(i);
            names1.add(mc.getName());
        }

        // (ii-a) Segment 1 rewritten using Stream
        List<String> names2 = list.stream()
            .map(Person::getName)
            .collect(Collectors.toList());

        System.out.println("All names (stream): " + names2);

        // -- Original Segment 2 (loop) ---------------------
        List<Person> persons1 = new ArrayList<>();
        for (int i = 0; i < list.size(); i++) {
            Person mc = list.get(i);
            if (mc.getAge() <= 20) persons1.add(mc);
        }

        // (ii-b) Segment 2 rewritten using Stream
        List<Person> persons2 = list.stream()
            .filter(p -> p.getAge() <= 20)
            .collect(Collectors.toList());

        System.out.println("Age <= 20 (stream): " + persons2);

        // (iii) Sort: ascending age, then ascending name
        list.sort(Comparator.comparingInt(Person::getAge)
                            .thenComparing(Person::getName));

        System.out.println("Sorted list: " + list);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
All names (stream): [Alice, Bob, Carol, Dave, Eve, Frank]
Age <= 20 (stream): [Bob, Carol, Dave, Eve]
Sorted list: [Eve(17), Bob(19), Carol(20), Dave(20),
              Alice(22), Frank(25)]
\end{verbatim}

\textbf{Key stream operations used:}
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item \texttt{.map(Person::getName)} --- transforms
  each \texttt{Person} to its name (method reference).
  \item \texttt{.filter(p -> p.getAge() <= 20)} ---
  keeps only persons aged $\leq 20$.
  \item \texttt{Comparator.comparingInt(...).thenComparing(...)}
  --- chains two comparators for multi-key sorting.
\end{itemize}

\end{tcolorbox}


\item Consider the \texttt{Fruit} class with \texttt{name} and \texttt{quantity}. Write Java code \\so that \texttt{Collections.sort(listFruits)} sorts by descending quantity; if equal, by lexicographic name. \mk{7}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2016--17, 2020--21}

%% ── Q4: Fruit Comparable sort ────────────────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cH!4,colframe=cH,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer — Fruit: Descending Quantity,
  Then Lexicographic Name}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cH]

\texttt{Collections.sort()} uses the natural ordering
defined by \texttt{Comparable<Fruit>}. We override
\texttt{compareTo()} to sort by
\textbf{descending quantity} first, then
\textbf{lexicographic (ascending) name}.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
import java.util.*;

class Fruit implements Comparable<Fruit> {
    private String name;
    private int    quantity;

    Fruit(String name, int quantity) {
        this.name = name; this.quantity = quantity;
    }
    public String getName()    { return name;     }
    public int    getQuantity(){ return quantity; }

    @Override
    public int compareTo(Fruit other) {
        // 1. Descending quantity
        int c = Integer.compare(other.quantity, this.quantity);
        if (c != 0) return c;
        // 2. Ascending (lexicographic) name
        return this.name.compareTo(other.name);
    }

    @Override
    public String toString() {
        return name + ":" + quantity;
    }
}

public class FruitDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        List<Fruit> listFruits = new ArrayList<>();
        listFruits.add(new Fruit("Mango",  10));
        listFruits.add(new Fruit("Apple",  25));
        listFruits.add(new Fruit("Banana", 25));
        listFruits.add(new Fruit("Grape",   8));
        listFruits.add(new Fruit("Cherry", 15));

        Collections.sort(listFruits);

        System.out.println(listFruits);
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
[Apple:25, Banana:25, Cherry:15, Mango:10, Grape:8]
\end{verbatim}

\textbf{Explanation:}
Apple and Banana both have quantity 25; they are
tied on quantity so they are sorted alphabetically
(Apple before Banana). Cherry (15), Mango (10),
Grape (8) follow in descending quantity order.

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Consider the following FIFA World Cup data. Declare Enumeration \texttt{FWCWinners}. Print all countries. Print the most recent winner (cannot simply write Argentina):
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lcc}
\toprule
\textbf{Country} & \textbf{Titles} & \textbf{Last Title}\\
\midrule
Argentina & 3 & 2022 \\
France & 2 & 2018 \\
Uruguay & 2 & 1950 \\
England & 1 & 1966 \\
Spain & 1 & 2010 \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2021--22}

%% ── Answer: FWCWinners enum ─────────────────────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cH!4,colframe=cH,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- \texttt{FWCWinners} Enumeration}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cH]

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
enum FWCWinners {
    ARGENTINA(3, 2022),
    FRANCE(2, 2018),
    URUGUAY(2, 1950),
    ENGLAND(1, 1966),
    SPAIN(1, 2010);

    private final int titles;
    private final int lastTitle;

    FWCWinners(int titles, int lastTitle) {
        this.titles = titles;
        this.lastTitle = lastTitle;
    }

    public int getTitles()    { return titles; }
    public int getLastTitle() { return lastTitle; }
}

public class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) {

        // Print all countries
        System.out.println("All FIFA World Cup Winners:");
        for (FWCWinners w : FWCWinners.values())
            System.out.println(w.name()
                + " | Titles: " + w.getTitles()
                + " | Last: " + w.getLastTitle());

        // Most recent winner (cannot simply write Argentina)
        FWCWinners recent = FWCWinners.values()[0];
        for (FWCWinners w : FWCWinners.values())
            if (w.getLastTitle() > recent.getLastTitle())
                recent = w;

        System.out.println("\nMost recent winner: " + recent.name()
            + " (" + recent.getLastTitle() + ")");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Output:}
\begin{lstlisting}
All FIFA World Cup Winners:
ARGENTINA | Titles: 3 | Last: 2022
FRANCE | Titles: 2 | Last: 2018
URUGUAY | Titles: 2 | Last: 1950
ENGLAND | Titles: 1 | Last: 1966
SPAIN | Titles: 1 | Last: 2010

Most recent winner: ARGENTINA (2022)
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item Consider the following EPL data. Write Java code to: (i) Declare a single Enumeration named \texttt{EPL}; (ii) Print all clubs with points and position:
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lcc}
\toprule
\textbf{Club} & \textbf{Point} & \textbf{Position}\\
\midrule
Manchester United & 90 & 1 \\
Chelsea & 80 & 2 \\

Manchester City & 30 & 19 \\
Liverpool & 25 & 20 \\

  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cH]

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
enum EPL {
    MANCHESTER_UNITED(90, 1),
    CHELSEA(80, 2),
    ARSENAL(75, 4),
    MANCHESTER_CITY(30, 19),
    LIVERPOOL(25, 20);

    private final int points;
    private final int position;

    EPL(int points, int position) {
        this.points = points;
        this.position = position;
    }

    public int getPoints()   { return points; }
    public int getPosition() { return position; }
}

public class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        // Print all clubs with points and position
        for (EPL club : EPL.values()) {
            System.out.println(club.name()
                + " | Points: " + club.getPoints()
                + " | Position: " + club.getPosition());
        }
    }
}

\item Declare Enumeration \texttt{GOT} for Game of Thrones characters. Find the character active for the least number of seasons (cannot simply write Ned Stark):
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lcc}
\toprule
\textbf{Name} & \textbf{Status} & \textbf{NoOfSeasons}\\
\midrule
Jon Snow & Alive & 7 \\
Daenerys Targaryen & Alive & 7 \\
Ned Stark & Dead & 1 \\
Joffrey Baratheon & Dead & 4 \\
Tyrion Lannister & Alive & 7 \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\yr{CSE 107 | 2016--17}

%% ── Answer: GOT enum + min seasons character ─────────────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cH!4,colframe=cH,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- \texttt{GOT} Enumeration: Least Active Character}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cH]

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
enum GOT {
    JON_SNOW("Alive", 7),
    DAENERYS_TARGARYEN("Alive", 7),
    NED_STARK("Dead", 1),
    JOFFREY_BARATHEON("Dead", 4),
    TYRION_LANNISTER("Alive", 7);

    private final String status;
    private final int seasons;

    GOT(String status, int seasons) {
        this.status = status;
        this.seasons = seasons;
    }

    public int getSeasons() { return seasons; }
}

public class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) {

        // Find character with least seasons (cannot simply write Ned Stark)
        GOT least = GOT.values()[0];
        for (GOT c : GOT.values())
            if (c.getSeasons() < least.getSeasons())
                least = c;

        System.out.println("Least active: " + least.name()
            + " (" + least.getSeasons() + " season(s))");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Output:}
\begin{lstlisting}
Least active: NED_STARK (1 season(s))
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}


\item What is a functional interface in Java? Give an example to implement the functional interface as an Anonymous Inner class. \mk{10}
\yr{CSE 201 | 2015--16}

%% ── Q5: Functional interface + Anonymous Inner Class ─────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cH!4,colframe=cH,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer — Functional Interface and
  Anonymous Inner Class}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cH]

\textbf{What is a functional interface?}

A \textbf{functional interface} is an interface that
contains \textbf{exactly one abstract method}. It
may have any number of \texttt{default} or
\texttt{static} methods, but only one abstract
method. The \texttt{@FunctionalInterface} annotation
enforces this contract at compile time.

Functional interfaces are the foundation of
\textbf{lambda expressions} and
\textbf{method references} in Java 8+. Examples
from the standard library include
\texttt{Runnable}, \texttt{Comparator<T>},
\texttt{Predicate<T>}, and \texttt{Function<T,R>}.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// Define a custom functional interface
@FunctionalInterface
interface MathOperation {
    int operate(int a, int b);   // single abstract method

    // default methods are allowed
    default void describe() {
        System.out.println("A math operation");
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{Example 1: Implement as an Anonymous Inner
Class}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
public class FunctionalDemo {
    public static void main(String[] args) {

        // Anonymous inner class implementing MathOperation
        MathOperation addition = new MathOperation() {
            @Override
            public int operate(int a, int b) {
                return a + b;
            }
        };

        MathOperation multiplication = new MathOperation() {
            @Override
            public int operate(int a, int b) {
                return a * b;
            }
        };

        System.out.println("5 + 3 = " + addition.operate(5, 3));
        System.out.println("5 * 3 = " + multiplication.operate(5, 3));
        addition.describe();
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Output:}
\begin{verbatim}
5 + 3 = 8
5 * 3 = 15
A math operation
\end{verbatim}

\medskip
\textbf{Example 2: Equivalent lambda expression
(Java 8+)}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
// Lambda is syntactic sugar for the anonymous class above
MathOperation subtraction = (a, b) -> a - b;
System.out.println("5 - 3 = " + subtraction.operate(5, 3));
\end{lstlisting}

\medskip
\textbf{Key points:}
\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item An anonymous inner class provides an
  instance of the interface without explicitly
  naming a class. It is verbose but works on all
  Java versions.
  \item A lambda expression is a concise replacement
  for a single-method anonymous class and is only
  available for functional interfaces.
  \item Both approaches are interchangeable for
  functional interfaces; the lambda is preferred
  in modern Java for readability.
\end{itemize}

\end{tcolorbox}

\item What is a functional interface? Using lambda expression, implement the following interface to compute factorial:
\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
interface SomeFunc<T> { T func(T t); }
\end{lstlisting}
\mk{10}
\yr{CSE 107 | 2015--16}

%% ── Answer: Functional interface + lambda factorial ─────────────────
\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced,breakable,ansbox,
  colback=cH!4,colframe=cH,boxrule=0.8pt,arc=5pt,
  title={\textbf{Answer --- Functional Interface \& Lambda: Factorial}},
  fonttitle=\bfseries\color{white},colbacktitle=cH]

A \textbf{functional interface} has exactly one abstract method.
The \texttt{@FunctionalInterface} annotation is optional but recommended.

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Java]
interface SomeFunc<T> { T func(T t); }

public class Main {
    public static void main(String[] args) {

        // Lambda expression implementing SomeFunc<Integer>
        SomeFunc<Integer> factorial = n -> {
            int result = 1;
            for (int i = 2; i <= n; i++)
                result *= i;
            return result;
        };

        System.out.println("5! = " + factorial.func(5));  // 120
        System.out.println("6! = " + factorial.func(6));  // 720
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Output:}
\begin{lstlisting}
5! = 120
6! = 720
\end{lstlisting}

\end{tcolorbox}

    MANCHESTER_UNITED(90, 1),
    CHELSEA(80, 2),

    MANCHESTER_CITY(30, 19),
    LIVERPOOL(25, 20);

        this.points = points;
        this.position = position;
    }

}

public class Main {

        // Cannot simply write 18 --- compute from enum data

                 - EPL.MANCHESTER_UNITED.getPosition();

\end{enumerate}

\markboth{S17 --- File I/O \& Serialization}{}
